RATING: 6
Highly thematic but you really need to understand all the cards, counters, special powers etc to play the game properly and to allow it to flow smoothly. Rating therefore is very tentative and whether an improved understanding will lead to a much richer game (and therefore higher rating) or just turn it into a one sided luck fest remains to be seen. I hope the former because it has lots of potential.

RATING: 6
Fun every now and again with the right group of folks. It has a lot of things I don't like: needless dice rolling, lazy design (specifically related to combat) and a whole bunch of randomness. Also one or two mechanics seem rather overpowered. Specifically, Dracula's ability to move anywhere on the board out of nowhere can cause the game to come to a grinding halt.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
After three plays, two as Dracula and one as the Hunters, I've decided that the game largely comes down to the presence or absence of a few powerful cards: Hypnosis, Devilish Power, Evasion, and a couple others. Any of these cards can, if they appear at the right time, swing the game completely in the other direction. For me this is too much chance and luck in a 3-hour game. I really wanted to like FoD; it's got a great theme and a unique mechanic with Dracula's trail. But it's no fun when the previous 2 hours of play are made irrelevant by a single card.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Dracula tries to rule the world. 4 Hunters must work together to find his hidden trail over whole europe. During nights Dracula is strong and might attack the hunters. During the days, the hunters can equip and prepare themselves for his encounters.

Draculas movement is hidden, so it's  abit like "scotland yard" finding his trail. With thematic encounters and event cards the hunters get on draculas trail quickly and a cat & mouse games begins.

The combat between dracula, his minions and the hunters is heavily based on luck and can ruin the game if you throw unlucky.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
Not really that fun in my estimation. I've been pressed into playing it a few times and will likely play again because those in my group really enjoy it. For me, the game just isn't mechanically interesting as it's basically hide-and-seek - with a combat system that is particularly droll. Dracula is always running for cover and the others are trying to get to the perfect cards that, once revealed, blow his cover and win them the game - after a lengthy and uninteresting number of moves to back Dracula into a corner. This sums up the entire game: "You move there, then I'll move here and then he can only go to that place or that one and I'll play a card that will reveal which place he's at and we'll have him." Every game leads to this precise statement. Sometimes, Dracula wins.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

This was fun! With 5 players it was nice, with two players not so much. Enjoyed it still, though.

The combat rules are a bit of a disappointment, perhaps I waited too much from this game...
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Hmm...I haven't really played this enough yet to say too much.  I expect that it's rating is more likely to go up a bit than down a bit.

Above all, this game is full of theme and atmospherics.  The designers did a great job with that.  Strip all of the chrome away and there's maybe not that much left, BUT the chrome is well done - and not too much for what we have.  It's kind of in the same area as Pirate's Cove I guess - the themes are very different but it's the same kind of fun, light-medium, bit of strategy/lots of theme sort of thing.  Where this one is not as good as that is in the fact that it can be MUCH slower to get to any sort of a climax.  Strategically, there's more going on, but when a fights start, PC is more edgy.

Some folks are going to want to knock this down for having too much chrome and not enough elegance or clever mechanisms (I can sense them sharpening their, ahem fangs, as I type), but actually I'll be fairly happy to see this periodically hit the table.

RATING: 7
I am a terrible Dracula but I shouldn't hold that against the game.  I think Letters from Whitechapel is easier on Jack than this game is for Dracula, but that could be the lack of experience we have as detectives in Whitechapel.

Either game is great fun.  One on many can cause hurt feelings in games like Descent (which is more confrontational).  This is just 'catch me if you can', but unlike Jack it is possible to fight back with Dracula.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Great components.  There is a lot going on in the game, however the special cards seem to be the key, either putting you on Dracula's trail or allowing him to teleport away.  The game is fun if the players keep it moving but if you are playing with analysis paralysis types it will drrraaaagggg. Having multiple people play the hunters doesnt particularly add/detract from the game since they have little to do individually on their turn and in combat your best play is generally straightforward and obvious. One caution: Alert the hunter players about the "Evasion" Dracula Card in the event deck, lest they flip out on you when it shows up.

RATING: 8
Definitely a preliminary rating - but the play we had was very entertaining! The many rules aren't so hard to manage if you watch Rahdo's video to get a strong idea of framework first, and then just flip through as you need them. So thrilled I was able to get a good secondhand copy, and it even came already sleeved.

Having had the chance to play it some more, I'm pleasantly surprised that, while it's not something I'd sit down and play twice in a row, we've been able to finish games under 2 hours without trying to rush. (I am reticent to teach the game to certain types of players with a lower attention span, though.) Both the hunters and Dracula have a great deal of fun. While more players helps, two player is a perfectly fine experience as long as the hunter player doesn't mind, perhaps thinking of it as having multiple units rather than having to take on the role of several players. Will eventually write down more specific and organized thoughts.

RATING: 8.5
Un jugador maneja a Drácula y el resto a los cazadores que tratan de darle caza por todo Europa. Drácula viaja en secreto, pero determinadas cartas u objetos de los cazadores pueden revelar localizaciones de su ruta, y hacerles ver a dónde puede haber ido. Faroleo, deducción y agobio mucho mucho agobio sobre todo si eres Drácula. No conozco juego que me agote tanto, en el buen sentido de la palabra, como este; más divertido y complicado ser Drácula, aunque de cazador supone tambien un reto. Buenos componentes, mucha ambientación.Tiene mucho azar, pero le viene bien para representar que hay que correr riesgos, que nunca vas a estar seguro de si haces bien en cada momento... Los combates son interesantísimos. Un juego diferente, para jugarlo por la noche y sumergirte en él.

I love the atmosphere, the hunt, the tricks and feints that both sides can pull, although I want to play it more before rating. My only concern is it seems to take a couple of plays to wade through the rules, unless there is an experienced teacher. 
Other than the occasional frustrating rule ambiguity, and the fact the designers missed the opportunity to make Whitby the UK mainland's northern port, this is fantastic.

A great game that offers two different playing experiences depending on which side you play.

The hunters get a cooperative-deduction game.  They have to coordinate their movements to cover different parts of the map, not only to narrow down Dracula's location but to clean up any new vampires he has left in his trail.  The hunters have different innate abilities and will collect different items and powers and players try to use them where they are best suited.

The Dracula player goes solo and must figure out a way to use his clever assortment of powers to evade the hunters -- not only to save himself but also to allow new vampires to mature before the hunters can find them.  

This is all built on a cool system where Dracula choses his movements by placing a trail of face-down cards.  At each location he can drop one of many different types of traps, or if he thinks that the hunters won't find it he can try to spawn a new vampire to help him win the game.

Dracula has other tricks besides the traps he places.  He can sometimes break movement rules by staying in one place while appearing to move.  Or jumping two spaces instead of one.  Or when desperate he can take a boat to one of many destinations.

Most of the time, the hunters are on the offensive when it comes to combat.  But in the right circumstances Dracula can try to kill a hunter by catching him alone, poorly armed, and at night.  This is a nice counter-threat and another way in which Dracula can win the game.

This is getting long, but I'll also mention that the combat system is really clever too.  Players simultaneously pick which weapons they are going to use, which match up in different ways.  I also like that the hunters control the flow of the event draw deck, but the cards can benefit either side.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

While I've enjoyed playing the "hunters", my only experience as Dracula was pretty boring. A lot of downtime while the others are planning (true, one has to listen and to learn how to outwit them, but since there are up to 2-3 options at any given time, I simply had to sit and wait).
So - I will probably want to play again, but not as the a-priory interesting role.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Fury of Dracula is easily one of my gaming group's favorite games. 

The game plays almost like a teamwork game where players try to beat the game, but instead all but one player is trying to beat the remaining player (Dracula). 

It is a game of hide and seek or cat and mouse...  Dracula moves about the board secretly while the other players try to find and destroy him. Players are constantly discussing where Dracula could be, how he got there, etc.

Dracula, while powerful, is best kept in the shadows. He can attack, but unless he has a really good reason (good chance of killing a player), he shouldn't... If he attacks it better be during the night when he is most powerful. We've learned that Dracula's best strategy is to remain a few steps ahead of the players and force them to encounter minions. Games always seem close, but it is extremely difficult to win as Dracula - which makes it very rewarding when you do! Usually we have one of the more experienced players be Dracula.

The game can last a long time - especially if the Dracula player is good at evasion and trickery. A typical game lasts 3 hours or longer. This game IS game night. Thankfully since it is a teamwork game, it is easy for a player to step out for a few rounds, while the other players play for him/her.

Great game. Fun theme. Excellent choice if you are looking for a new game to bring to the table!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This game is great fun.  As Dracula, there is nothing more satisfying than to slip right through the hunters' fingers and watch them spend the next two rounds trying to figure out how you escaped their "perfect" trap.

On the hunter side, it is electrifying to have the dark prince cornered, the sun rising, and only a trip out to sea left for him to desperately contemplate.

Bluff, timing, and resource management are the hallmarks of this game.  Knowing how the combat cards interact (especially what happens when you LOSE the combat roll) is key to maximizing Fury's fun potential.  The game plays best with 3 players, in my opinion.  This is my favorite medium-length game.

Edit: After dozens of plays, I have to bump Drac down a few points.  The endgame Resolve-powered teleport festival is annoying and unthematic.  3rd Edition is superior.

Volt, hogy ugyanazokat a lapokat tudtuk csak kijátszani hosszú körökön át a küzdelem során, és szinte kizárólag a kockadobásról szólt a dolog. ---
Második játékban én voltam Dracula. Továbbra sem tetszik a harc, bár ennek az oldalnak több a lehetősége. Túl nagy a szerencse szerepe, a kártyák, lapkák és a kockadobás miatt.

RATING: 6.5
Fury of Dracula is the ameritrash twin of Scotland Yard.
The premise is the same: one versus all in a hunt, but in this game the prey has fangs! And, at night, you don't really want to catch it...

The game is very thematic, but it is a bit too long. And much of its length comes from a convoluted and baroque combat system based on cards, that is often too long in achieving any result.

I'd like the idea, but it really shows its age: all the micro-rules, while thematic, are a chore to bear in mind. And many of the things this game does well, Letters from Whitechapel does better...

RATING: 3
I found Fury of Dracula stupidly random.  Where is the strategy?  The outcome of almost every action that I made was determined by chance.  For example, you never knew if drawing an event card would benefit the Hunters or Dracula.  Travel by train to either corner Dracula or lose your turn based on a stupid die roll.  I'm not even going to get into the lame 6-sider/card combat system.

Anyway, The event cards seriously hampered Dracula.  His initial board position was too easy to deduce.  On turn 2 the hunters were able to reveal his last location.  During the next few turns we drew 2 other event cards that revealed too much of his path.  Perhaps I was expecting a more challenging version of Scotland Yard.  

Actually a better question is "Where's the narrative?"  My experience went something like this... Van Helsing visits Vienna.  Dracula is not there.  Van Helsing attempts to board a train.  He is delayed.  Van Helsing then encounters Thieves who steal his pistol.  Next Van Helsing encounters Dracula and punches him in the mouth, but Dracula manages to dodge a stake to the heart.  To me, this sounds like a pretty boring narrative, but I guess there are some people who would probably love this storyline.

RATING: 10
The game is not perfect, but once you take the time to learn it forwards and back, it's an amazing game. No other hidden movement games I've played allow the hurted to become the hunter, then reverse those roles every few turns. 

While 3rd is prettier and has some improvements(cards rather than chits), they broke some key elements, namely several turns at day, then several at night.

Game is a 10, not because it's perfect, but because of what it's been to me. It was my 1st "designer" board game and was played for hours and hours before I ever branched out into other games.

RATING: 9
I've played this four times so far, and have really enjoyed it despite losing every time.  The action and rules are perfectly suited for the theme, and the mechanics are well thought out and cohesive enough to provide a satisfying play experience every time, even when the players employ a variety of strategies.  That being said, the game has some obvious weaknesses, chief among them the odd combat system that *seems* like it offers some strategic options, but all too often just comes down to a roll-off.  

Later: Aw, fuck it.  This game is AWESOME and who am I to fight it?  Yeah, the combat can be a little wonky, but more often than not it's quick and satisfying.  Yeah, there's a touch of crazy randomness, but who cares?  It's fun, it's simple, it's Dracula vs. the vampire hunters, it's everything it should it be.

RATING: 8
The Fury of Dracula is all about theme: you really can see the story unfold in a fashionable way as the hunters retrace Dracula’s trail and close in on him. All in all it feels like one of those black and white movies of old that develop on both atmosphere and mystery rather than a special effects and CGI modern piece of trash, which is rather surprising but deeply appeasing as well.

With a pun that only works in Italian, we think «La fuga di Dracula» (Flight of Dracula) sounds more appropriate a title than «La furia di Dracula» (Fury of Dracula) as the only thing the eponymous character had better do is fleeing from the start.

RATING: 8
Have introduced it to my school students. I raised its rating as it proved an even better game than I originally thought. If you like deduction games with some race and combat strategies thrown in, this is a game you would love. Not a euro in the area of calculating pathways to victory but a lot more psychology. It's very tense as Dracula!

The FFG components are spectacular as well. I've played the original GW version when I was younger. I prefer this ones' card system for Dracula's path. A destination card plus the encounter on top. This allows for encounters to be revealed but not the destination and vicea versa, as well as the hunters to prepare better or be mislead to the importance of the destination.

RATING: 9
This game can really create a lot of tension.  Between the cat-and-mouse hunt and the way that cards are drawn from the bottom of the deck, this can be a real edge of your seat game.  It can also be a little slow, but I find that to be the case if you aren't playing correctly (c'mon, Dracula player, ATTACK MINA!!!).  The combat needs to be seen from both sides before you can even begin to fully comprehend it (which I'm okay with for my own evil reasons), and when you do get it, you find that it's the kind of combat that while, yes, you need the dice on your side, you also need a solid strategy (in this case, trying to predict what the opponent will play) in place first.

One of my most favorite games.

I suspect that Dracula needs to make a kill the first night then run away like crazy after that in order to win.

With a game collection like mine, I doubt this is going to hit the table again, as I have a large number of games I`d rather play over this one.

RATING: 7
No soy muy amigo de los cooperativos, y este lo es. No obstante,es un juego entretenido. Admite hasta cinco jugadores, de los cuales, uno necesariamente ha de ser drácula y el resto cazadores que deben encontrarlo y matarlo en alguna de las ciudades de europa que vienen en el tablero. Los cazadores se van desplazando por el tablero. En cambio, el movimiento de drácula es oculto y viene determinado por unas cartas (boca abajo) que van determinando su ruta. En el momento que un cazador visita una ciudad de la ruta, la carta de ruta se desvela y permite hacerse una idea de por donde puede andar drácula. Además, en las ciudades, drácula puede ir dejando "regalitos". Los cazadores se van haciendo de objetos y desvelando eventos según van viajando por europa. 

El juego termina con victoria para drácula si aguanta 6 días sin ser eliminado o el contador de vampiros llega a 6.

Es entretenido. Tiene deducción. Los combates se resuelven con un método tipo piedra-papel-tijera.

RATING: 8
Nice adaptation of the hidden movement mechanic, with great theme. Long, though we are learning as we become familiar with the rules and strategy. We all enjoyed the experience, which seems very balanced with field of search not to expansive with the number of hunters. Brilliant mechanic of having the encounters hamper the hunters, while they are needing to challenge them to find new vampires and reduce scoring opportunities for the Dracula player. At the same time, Dracula attempts to battle hunters at key moments while staying hidden. Event card play provides the right amount of correction to keep the game from being stalled, yet not too overpowering. Battle resolution has a fresh approach, and gives the game a break from the search mode. Rate an 8 for a few overpowered cards in the deck. The blood flows as bullets are dodged and holy water is used in an attempt by hunters to vanquish the beast.

RATING: 6
The final result is less than the sum of its parts. It does neither the cat-n-mouse component, nor the combat very well.

That is too bad because the theme is super fantastic and fits the mechanics. It's a good idea to elevate the cat-and-mouse genre above Scotland Yard.

But that component is weak. The map is relatively simple and the chase is not that exciting.

But where the game really falls apart is the combat system. It's lame...and we were indifferent as to the outcome of the fight. We efforted a group fight, but Dracula could just pick on one person to pound on, while the others in the group just watch. That's a lousy and unbelievable narrative.

At the end of the day, I will gladly reach for Letters from Whitechapel. But FoD will likely get a future pass.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
Ahh, so much promise, so little payoff.  This has to be my biggest disappointment thus far in the world of gaming.  Combine the mechanism of Scotland Yard (one of my childhood faves) with a theme I love (any horror, really, but literary themes are cool), and I was excited.  And in theory, the game should be great.  The theme and the mechanism work good together, the art is great (as per much FFG product) but - it's just not fun.  At least, not for two.  The game seems to take an eternity to get going, with the hunters blindly thrashing around Europe.  If by chance they bump into Drac, then great, we're off and running, but if the Dracula player is any good, it's not hard to evade for quite a while - and as far as I'm concerned, 4 or 5 cities deep on the trail is quite a head start.  Basically, unless you stumble onto Dracula or get a good card draw, it'll be quite a while before any combat occurs.  The encounters with the followers are just ok.  The system for hunter/Dracula combat is pretty cool, and lots of fun, but unless you get a bunch of hunters together in a joint battle (which is pretty damn hard to pull off), Dracula can often win (or escape) with ease.  So essentially, a lot of ho-hum and waiting around, for a few minutes of actual fun.  We tried the game once with 5, and even then, it was pretty lame, and our guests were unimpressed.  We felt bad for making them play, and after that, I sold it off.  Maybe someone else more dedicated than I can hone a strategy that leads to some fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I really like this game. Sure, I wish it were a bit shorter, but it's a lot of fun and very thematic. It may be better with fewer players (3, maybe). 5 seems a touch thin; not a lot for the hunters to do individually, and the game time balloons as much discussion takes place. Also, you need a wily Dracula who is familiar with all the options; playing Dracula requires more familiarity with the game than playing the hunters.

Couple tips for the Dracula player:

Your strategy will depend a lot on the initial disposition of the hunters. A common initial Hunter setup is to put one hunter in each corner of the board, and then work their way towards the center. This makes sense, because the peripheries of the board are easier to search earlier than later. But, if they go this route, you can set up near one of the isolated hunters and try to kill them the first night. Remember, hunters will only get stronger as the game goes on, while you will tend to get weaker. If you can pick someone off the first night, that means by the dawn of the second day you're halfway to winning. It can be somewhat risky, but unless a hunter gets lucky on the weaponry in the first few turns, they can't do a lot to you.

If the Hunters set up concentrated in the middle and work their way outwards, your job will be a little tougher, although they most likely won't discover you for a little longer. Use that time to set up a New Vampire (use Dark Call if necessary to get one) and lay down a web of encounter tokens. Then, while the Hunters have to split up to deal with both you and your New Vampire, try to isolate one hunter at night and kill them. This may be tricky, as the Hunters will likely be better-armed; try to accumulate a couple good combat cards, and find someone with a weak selection of items. When in doubt, go after Mina; you can kill her with a single bite. You should have a few chances to look at the Hunters' hands; be careful if they have enough combat cards to hurt you.

Dracula is extremely powerful at night, but ridiculously weak during the day. This will drive your tactics. Attack at night and escape as a bat (using either Escape as Bat or Fangs) to open up some distance and uncertainty. A common use of  your Wolf Form card is to evade, but always remember you can also use it to attack - if you can use the Wolf Form to make an attack first thing in the evening, you can potentially hound one hunter for a couple turns until you kill him or her.

Dracula must combine guile and aggression to win. I don't think you can pull it off if you're just hiding and trying to mature New Vampires. The process is too slow, and experienced, well-armed hunters are going to catch up with you eventually (against inexperienced hunters, you can win this way though).

Our very early games saw Dracula winning, but then the Hunters went on a long and impressive winning streak. But once Dracula started playing aggressively, especially early, the Hunters have been routinely getting beaten badly again, and haven't quite found the adjustment yet.

RATING: 4
I'll start with the good.  1) Hunting down Dracula is a hell of a lot of fun.  The Trail mechanic is amazing.  Using the Trail to mature vampires in a particular city is fun as well.  2) Good theme and intense at times.  3) Nice production values.
The Bad: 1) This game feels broken.  Dracula should not have 2 step escape routes without being able to pick up his trail.  You can spend 2 hours pinning him down only to have him escape as a bat or use wolf form and suddenly he's on the other side of the map.  Don't even get me started on that teleporter card, that's just ridiculous.  2) The game is waaay to long. 3) I think the comat system is much too complicated for what it is - which is really just rolling one die a piece and seeing who has a higher number.  4) Even if you do manage to find and fight Dracula more than twice in under three hours, you can't hurt him unless you have the right items - but he has a bunch of cards to remove your items.  I think the cards are unbalanced.   Overall: I am dying for a game that utilizes the Hide and Seek/Trail mechanic that plays in 90 minutes or less, but this game gets bogged down in extraneous messy abilities.

RATING: 3
Somewhat difficult to rate, this is a thematic game, and is clearly based on rules that are home more in the 80's than the aughts, but ultimately it left me with a feeling of "meh."

Most people are probably familiar with the premise: asymmetrical sides: one player is dracula, the others are hunters. The hunters try to corner dracula and kill him in hand to hand, dracula tries to slink around and leave traps for the players.

Now, about the gameplay though, the problem to me, like many older style games, is that there just isn't very much to do on a given turn. A lot of the game for the non-dracula players seems to be driven by walking or taking trains to European locales, and then drawing some cards, some of which are useful to you, some of which go to the drac player. There are occasional flashes of potential excitement, when drac is spotted for instance, but the player characters seem to move agonizingly slowly and it seemed difficult to get the count in spots where you could actually take it to him in combat. Apparently, that is some of the idea of the game, because dracula, while adequate in combat, isn't any great shakes either.

What seems to be left, after all of that, is a game where most of the time players sit around drawing cards and, occasionally, rolling dice. While the board, the cards, and the character design ooze theme, the actual gameplay on this left me bored. It's not a bad design, but there just isn't enough going on to make it very interesting. Frankly, I would rather play multiple games of Clue: The Great Museum Caper in the same time...it's a more fun game that plays in a fraction of the time. It'll also cost you about 1/3 as much on the secondary market, and it has many more meaningful choices per game than this one while still maintaining the best of the game mechanics that this one has to offer.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Next to AH's DUNE, this is my favorite game of all time, a perfect mix of proper Hammer-style gothic horror and a compelling mystery game with ample doses of strategy, suspense, and unpredictability.  FFG's version improves many elements of the gameplay, chiefly by employing a few new mechanics to put a little more pressure on Dracula as well as the hunters- overall, there's a greater sense of urgency and the game isn't able to descend into the 4 hour "where the hell is he" turkey shoots the original version could.  It's much more about tracking Dracula rather than finding him, and as a result it seems like there is a lot more opportunities for the hunters to collude and conspire to even the odds in their favor.  The other new elements, such as allies and the card-based movement all work a charm and the cludgy but endearing tables and charts of the original are rendered obsolete.  Mina is a great 5th hunter and her "questionable past" with Dracula makes the cards affecting bitten hunters almost always useful.  Dracula's special abilities are devious and fun or frustrating depending on which side of the fangs you fall.  The art is top notch, although I do miss the old GW style.  There is literally nothing I don't adore about this game.  I could say that I think the "Sense of Emergency" ability is a little too powerful or that Dracula is almost too easy to find in some situations, or that the Catacombs aren't as useful as it seems like they should be, but I could really care less.  This is a game that I love, it's a theme I love, and it's back in print in a beautiful, well-considered version with thoughtful and respectful revisions that maintain the tone and texture of the original while making it modern and exciting even after nearly 20 years.

RATING: 4
I went into this somewhat begrudgingly, becuase I've some to realize that I just don't like 2 things:
1) cooperative games.
2) card-driven games.
That said, I didn't "not like" it as much as I expected. That ability for players to share all their information with each other is like fresh air after games like Shadows Over Camelot. As is the role of Dracula, where he actually gets some meaningful choices, rather than just pretend he's not the bad guy, like in SoC. So, this was one of the less painful games for me in an intersection of genres that I don't care for. So that's probably like an 8 or 9 for people who like those genres.

RATING: 9
Played two 4-player games last night. While they were both learning games, they were still completely engaging. This game would seem to hold a lot of promise (in my group, at least)... an immersive theme, lots of strategic choices. I think this one's going to be a real winner!

UPDATE: This has quickly become another group favorite. It's always interesting, always exciting, always fun to play. While I haven't played it with two, it plays VERY well with 3, 4 and 5 players. It's almost always requested when our group numbers 5 or fewer. Each game plays out differently, the options for players' strategies are quite varied, and the sheer number of events that can occur can swing the game wildly to one or another side's favor. And I've never seen so much as a flicker of boredom cross a single player's face in any of the games we've played... which makes me think Fury Of Dracula will be hitting the table often and for a long time to come!

RATING: 6
7.5 This is could be the top performer for the coop genre. 

Compared to Shadows over camelot it is more complicated, but also much more rewarding. 
Compared to Descent I would say it is more satisfying for the amount of time spent (ratio). 

The component quality is first rate and there are many game systems. 

I'm not giving it a higher rating becuase of the following: the rules are overcomplicated, though they do provide depth. There are errors in a couple of the big combat cards (see errata), this should have been caught, or covered in an expansion upgrade or fixup pack. The combat system needs a playmat to help players understand flow. The combat system is over designed with something like 166 possible outcomes, making it a hard system to learn -- normally this much choice would be a good thing, but there is a heavy luck element layered overtop the choice array, which marginalizes intentionality too much. 40 + dice would have done fine. 

Play enjoyment definetly improves with experience as you figure out what the rules really mean and are able to play with more intent. I would definetly buy any expansion pack if one came out.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
A really interesting deduction game of "hunter-and-prey" style with lots of nasty surprises, tension and very special atmosphere. Here one player, tricky Count Dracula acts against all other players who are called The Hunters. Hunters cooperate with each other, discuss their plans and make their guesses, but The Evil always is nearby. It sits at the other side of the table, listens very carefully and secretly makes its insidious move, which will ruin this nice strategy built by the hunters a minute ago.

Usually people who didn't have good experience with this game say, that it relies too much on a dice throw. They say, that Dracula sometimes is easily killed when he has not luck with the dices. That's true, but the dices become that important only when direct conflict with Dracula occurs. And that is something that should be avoided by all means. The game is much more about seeking and hunting then about kicking, shooting and staking.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A remake of the very good Games Workshop game of the mid 80's.  Dracula (of the novel, not the movies) romps around Europe on a hidden map, trying to raise a tribe of Vampires, while the (now) four hunter players try to stop ol' toothy.  Early days with the new one, but lots has changed.  Dracula now has a sliding track of the last six locations visited, and vampires are now "matured" when they slide off the track (i.e. they have to survive six turns on the board to count).  There are now four hunters, instead of the original three - the fragile Mina appears.  This makes the board appear very small to Dracula, however his paper trail of encounters has shrunk as well, and can shrink further if he sires a vampire.  Other new rules are Ally cards that help both sides, Catacombs to store encounters that have moved off the track, special power cards for both sides.  Missing rules are the messy blood death/castle Dracula endgame, hunters becoming vampires, and the instant kill with a stake.  Dracula isn't killed instantly with a stake anymore - rather he's worn down.  All these changes appear to help quicken the playing time, ramp up the interaction, and break the rather boring cycle of Newspaper Reports/Evasion of the original game.  I was initially worried by the changes, having logged around 40  games of the 1986 version, but it appears to work while keeping the excellent atmosphere of the original.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7

RATING: 5
Played this game with high expectations at BGG.con 2014. Results: We had fun but I don't know why this game is so highly regarded, let alone sitting in the top 500. 

For one thing the combat is needlessly complex and paradoxically too simple. If you have all these special cards and abilities, why does it come down to a simple 1v1 toss of a d6? 

For another thing, the game already has a pretty long run time and there are cards that just frustrate everyone. Like letting Dracula jump to any spot on the map. As Dracula, I drew this card and decided against using it. It's basically an "add one hour of gameplay" card! And there are others that strip the players of their hard-won items and so forth. 

As a huge fan of Dracula and gothic horror, I just felt let down after hearing so many good things about Fury. If you aren't sold on the theme, I'd say just go get Whitechapel - it'll save you about 150 bucks and many hours. 

That said, if FFG decides to update and re-release this game, I think there's a big chance for an improvement.

RATING: 6
Whitechapel pretty much fired this game from my collection. While there are some admirable aspects to it (I quite like the way cards are drawn in a push-your-luck manner) and the theme is rendered quite well, there's too much useless hidden movement and deduction due to too many cards that reveal Dracula's whereabouts. 

If Whitechapel didn't exist, I'd make a variant to remove most if not all of those cards and force the hunters to expend Resolve to reveal a location card. As it is, the board is just too small to hide for very long, and the way location cards are revealed removes way too much of the deduction element for me. It's not uncommon for most of Dracula's movements to be revealed or easily deduced from other revealed cards. I found it frustrating to make a clever move only to have the hunters play a card to have me reveal myself. Why play a deduction game then?

Otherwise, I find the game reasonably balanced and the combat doesn't bother me like it bothers some (hey, combat is iffy; proceed at your own risk). But if I want to play a deduction game and match wits, I'd much prefer Whitechapel.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This atmospheric murdery deduction game is best played by candlelight when a storm takes out the electricity.

Dracula's trail of map location cards is well implemented and is one of my favorite game mechanics.  The card driven combat system, on the other hand, seems overwrought, repetitive, tedious, and unnecessarily time-consuming.  Because combat is so "swingy," even sound strategies often end unpredictably and abruptly which can make the conclusion unsatisfying.  Nevertheless, the game of cat and mouse leading up to that conclusion is always a good time. 

In my experience, this game is heavily weighted in favor of Dracula and the hunters have a very slim chance of winning unless Dracula is assigned some form of handicap.

RATING: 8
Be prepared for a long play for the first game, though the speed of play improves with familiarity with the cards, and there are a lot in FoD.  In fact, it really helps to have at least two people who know the game, one to play dracula and the other to play one of the hunters and coach the other hunters.

Also, this game seems to bog down and become mundane for the hunters until they find Dracula's trail.  But when they do, it becomes a tense cat and mouse experience of evasion and deduction.

Overall, this is a great game, very immersive and atmospheric, and especially fun for all as the hunters do finally close in on the count.

RATING: 8
The single most thematic board game I have ever played. It simulates the main concept of Bram Stoker's novel perfectly: a dark core of hidden evil which manifests infrequently and indirectly. This game could be considered a dungeon crawler, where Europe is the dungeon, cities are rooms and Dracula's traps are the encounters. The difference is that the dungeon master in somewhere on the map, both as prey and boss monster. The production is what you would expect from FFG, gothic eye-candy. But the gameplay is marred by another thing I came to expect from FFG: a clunky card-driven combat system. It is counterintuitive and slows the already long game a lot, diminishing the goodwill of potential players. The game begs for a streamlined combat system, maybe with specialized dice. It would subtract one hour from expected play time and bring this game to a 10 on my list.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Played 1 time with 3 players. A rating for 4 may seem a bit harsh, and even I admit that it is surprisingly low. I don't feel that it should be a 4, but let me a bit more. The Good: it has nice components, lots of really neat ideas in the mechanics (Dracula's trail, combat system, encounter chips with smaller battles), and great theme. The Bad: it is really long, and the end seems sort of anti-climactic. If Scotland Yard didn't exist, I might not have minded so much, but Scotland Yard provides the tension of the hunt without all the slow and frustrating parts (the search for a lost trail, the Evasion card). I like the extra mechanics in FoD, but don't feel they add enough enjoyment to the game to make it worth a 3 hour investment. I like the game, but would prefer to play 1 game of Scotland Yard followed by two other games, than the 1 game of FoD that the same block of time would provide. Which means I don't want to play it often. Which means it must be a 4.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
One thing I have read often in the comments is that for a lot of games, the theme seems pasted on.  If there is a game where the theme is blended perfectly with the mechanics and the play of the game, this is certainly it.  The growing frustration with which the hunters must scurry around is tangible; the ephemerous omnipotence of the Count soon transforms into a delicate form of sacrifice to nudge forward; the scope and travel through Europe ressembles a wicked treasure hunt against time.  Great great game.  The options are plentiful for the Count but he must be careful not to come out in the sun to often.  Fight seldom and never in the day against a well-stocked hunter.  The call of the sea can be alluring but be warned that Storms do happen and sometimes in the worst of times.  Exquisite suspense.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Strong theme and easy to learn, with a high amount of interactivity (among the hunters, anyway) and a great sense of drama and narrative. Works well as a long 2-player game, if the Hunter player doesn't mind keeping track of 4 different hands of cards. Still, naturally, the more the merrier. In 4-player games, we've started putting the 4th Hunter (usually Van Helsing) under joint control of all the players, which seems easier than sticking one player with two. (Actually, this is a great game for two couples to play.)

The variety of event cards, item cards and encounters makes the replay value quite high.  The amount of detail and flavor in the cards and encounters really heighten the game's atmosphere, the same way that the little details in a book or movie make it more believable.

This is a pretty fiddly game, especially in combat. Still, it's easy to grasp for newer gamers, especially in contrast to Arkham Horror, Battlestar Galactica and some of FFG's other narrative-driven games. Just put them on the Hunter team, give them Seward or Van Helsing, and they'll be in good shape.

RATING: 7
A cat and mouse game where Dracula must hide from the rest of the players and sometimes attack one of them to get points. In the meantime, he leaves along the way some of his followers to make things harder for the hunters. These ones must do teamwork based on deduction to know where Dracula can be, to attack and kill him. 

Lots of cards, reactions, unpredicatable twists, Ameritrash-like. Life points, weapons, combats... 

This game can be tense but on the other hand some people may find it boring in case hunters don't find Dracula. I've always played Dracula and enjoyed all the games. Hunters in my games usually have liked it too. 

Game can be long, though, 3 hours or more...

RATING: 8
This is a great 5 player game. On the cuteness meter it would be a 10, but as an old wargamer I'd prefer the sides to be a bit more asymmetrical. Perhaps, the Count could have been given a + 1 DRM at Midnight and the hunter's a + 1 DRM at High Noon. The game is also unbalanced, but that's not usually the game breaker you would think because which side should win isn't consistent. Namely, the game lasts a maximum of 6 "days", if it goes 5 or 6 days the Count is toast, if it goes 2 or 3 days he has a great chance to win. An experienced and clever Count can win by using all his powers as often as possible, using dark call early to maximize his powerful encounters, attacking Mina and being devious. For example, he could force the occasional hunter toward his hidden location, or use wolf form to change directions or he could stay at sea at night to give a new vampire about to mature a fighting chance if discovered. His possibilities are endless, but he has to use them all to win. 
  What can spoil the game is the untimely appearance of the "Evasion" card. Every once in a while this card will show up just as all four hunters have cornered the Count. Once he teleports, the hunters are dead. They have no idea where he is, it's near the end of the game and even if they can figure out where he's gone it will take them forever to get there. And even then he's had more than enough time to bolt from there anyway. 

All in all, an entertaining game most of the time. 

For a more detailed analysis of this game see our site "The Boardgaming Life."

RATING: 8
[b][i]Fury of Dracula[/i][/b] is a deduction game set 8 years after Bram Stoker's story, but with the same characters. Thematic gameplay is effected by the story and fantastic components, particularly the game board. This game is strategical. Finding and cornering Dracula requires planning--Dracula is a slippery beast. It's exciting for both sides to have the investigators think they're closing in on Dracula only to discover he's slipped their net. Moments such as this make a fun and memorable game.

Some of the abilities seem overly powerful and so I'd recommend exploring a few of the variants listed in the Files page after you've tried the base game a few times. The box says 2--5 players, but I think it shines with 2 or, best of all, 3.

RATING: 5.5
A thematic remake of Scotland Yard.  Using four hunters you track Dracula across Europe trying to kill him before he survives long enough to raise new mininions or kills enough hunters.  Unlike Scotland Yard, Fury adds in additional luck elements such as event cards that can be good or bad, as well as item cards for hunters to use.  In Scotland Yard you just have to find the bad guy, in Fury of Dracula you have to find and kill him before being killed. This game just has a bit too much "chrome" for me.  It focuses a little bit too much about telling a story than being the deduction game that is its heart.  If you have people who are into the Dracula theme and like detective games then this would be a good choice, but for more pure Euro players then Scotland Yard is a better pick.

RATING: 9
More complex that other hidden identity games like Scotland Yard or Letters from Whitechaple, this game contains a LOT OF GAME. There is so much going on. Aside from being a busy affair, it drips the Dracula theme like blood from a fang.
Someone gets the lucky task of playing the infamous Count from Bram Stoker's fiction, and sneaks around Europe trying to start a new race of super, sexy vampires or possibly the next generation of salon hair stylist. The rest of the players take on the role of adversaries called "hunters" and/or "Lunch" who find clues to the spawn of Satan's whereabouts and ultimately encounter Dracula or his minions in bloody combat. It will take a few play-throughs to get the grasp of the rules and mechanics, but once you're past that, this game is a real nail-biter of tension as every choice leads you closer to victory or defeat.
If you love Gothic games, and you're planning on throwing a killer game-themed Halloween party, try to track it down. If nothing else, set it up on your living room table and watch people drool as they pass by.

RATING: 6

*** UPDATE ***
I have nearly 6-7 games under my belt now as Dracula (hope to play as a Hunter soon), I lost only once but every time victories were more difficult to achieve. In my last game I lost with Dracula killed in Rome's dusk. What an epic game it has been! Dirty tricks were the rule on both sides... this is a wonderful, devilish piece of a game.

*** UPDATE ***
Now I have 20 or so games under my belt. The game's still a refreshing experience!

*** UPDATE ***
Ok I've played this game A LOT, maybe too much. Some things don't come into place: combat for instance is a little too random for me - even if weapon choices really affect combat, but you need to have the game to study it, most people don't have it and cannot bother to read the strategy guides. VERY STEEP learning curve! You end up never having skilled adversaries especially if the Dracula player is YOU.
I'll give it a "9" now.

*** UPDATE ***
I got tired of this game. For some reason no matter if I win or lose I feel empty and bare after this game.
I feel tired and in a bad mood, not satisfied as I should be after a fun session.
For instance: "In the Shadow of the Emperor" I play quite often but after play I'm amused and happy of the experience I had. Not for FoD.
I'll give it a "7" which is a great deal away from the "9" I gave it at first.

RATING: 6.5
If I had a regular group of "heavy" gamers to play this with (plus a babysitter for our 19 month old), I think it would be one of my favorites.  However, most of the time, it's just me and my wife.  While it is playable and fun with two, the person controlling 4 hunters is a bit overwhelmed with all of the equipment to keep track of.  There are LOTS of cardboard bits and several different types of cards, so the game is very fiddly.  

I really really want to like this game because I LOVE the secret movement and Dracula hunting aspect of the game.  It's so exciting to stumble across Dracula's trail and deal with whatever traps he has left for you.  However, the combination of needy toddler, 2 players most of the time, and relative depth of the game (tried it once with friends but they didn't like it much) brings me to rate this 6.5.  

I really want to like this game, but if we do not find another couple of "heavy" gamers soon, it is going to be traded or sold to make room for others.

RATING: 7
Fun game - one against many is a nice change from other games.  The theme of the game is used with good effect.

While you can play with any number of hunter players (1-4); Dracula will have the hardest time against all 4 as playing multiple hunters makes it more difficult to remember all of the spots you have been.

In some ways, this game is almost like an RPG with Dracula as the GM.  Given a smart group of hunters, I think Dracula has some long odds, but maybe it is more about making a challenge for the hunters, rather than 'winning'.

Not perfect, as the game is bit long if Dracula goes the distance.  I can see the hunters start to get bored when Dracula is doing well.  There is also alot of luck; while the event card luck can be managed, the combat dice luck can be a problem.

rating is '8' as dracula, '7' as a hunter.

painted miniatures

RATING: 8
A fun game that is heavy with theme. The four hunters from Bram Stoker's novel pursue Dracula across Europe, hoping to destroy him once and for all. 

Gameplay is quick and each turn passes swiftly. At the same time, there are decisions to be made and you may need to use some logic and guesswork to pinpoint Dracula's location. 

As time goes by, you really start to feel the pressure build to the climax. Will Dracula infest all of Europe? Or will the courageous heroes vanquish him and his cursed spawn? Only you can decide!

RATING: 9
This game generates a vivid story that explores Dracula’s complexity. He is a predator who feeds off humans and who can command terrifying power. But he is also completely dependent on and vulnerable to humanity. He is weak during the day. To spawn new vampires, he needs to plant them somewhere difficult to find, where they lie completely vulnerable. As hunters track the spawn, Dracula is often faced with the choice of making himself bait so as to distract the hunters. He needs to lure the hunters away from the spawn, but at the same time he needs to watch out that he doesn’t get killed. Sometimes Dracula can weary of running, and decide to take a stand and bring the story to its decisive moment. Sometimes the only way for his bride to mature is for him to run. 

The hunters fight the clock to catch Dracula and his spawn. They can wield great powers that limit what Dracula can do, that make certain options too costly for Dracula to pursue. They can find him out by tracking but also with the help of allies and rumours. But he can be anywhere, and sometimes when he is about to be caught, he slips away. Sometimes when he is nowhere to be found, he is revealed. When hunters close in, they must move as fast as they can before Dracula escapes, but they must also uncover any sleeping brides waiting to mature into vampires. When hunters are weak, they can team up and become formidable, but this limits their ability to search new places. 

***

What a fantastic game. I like pressing my luck with Dracula: circling close to lay traps, tempting hunters to keep chasing me instead of resting, attacking at nightfall.

I completely disagree wtih complaints that this game is complex. The rules are VERY simple and straightforward. 

Extremely vivid atmosphere. Games can be very tense.

RATING: 7
A refreshing coop game, where 4 players try to track down and kill Dracula.  The Dracula player has a deck of cards which s/he uses to move secretly about the board, while at the same time setting up encounters/traps for the other players.  Dracula's objective is to "mature" vampires and stay alive long enough to accumulate 6 Vampire points.  Everyone else tries to prevent this from happening.

The move/action sequence plays really fast, and there is no down time unless there is combat.  Once combat starts, it can be somewhat tedious if you don't have the right item(s), so it may be best to run to fight another day.  The combat system is "blow-by-blow", which makes it last a little longer, but it's entertaining to watch, initially anyways.

If you like "Mr. X" or "Scotland Yard" type games, this one comes highly recommended.

My copy did have one unfortunate problem; the counter sheet was not punched thoroughly, thus most of the encounter tokens where damaged when we tried to punch them out.  We even tried using an xacto, but that didn't help.  :(

I wrote to FFG and they promptly sent me a replacement flat!  Excellent customer service!!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Playing Dracula is challenging and a lot of fun!

RATING: 5
This game is incredible beautiful & the most thematic game i've ever had.. but it has a problem. The age shows.. meaning the gameplay is somewhat outdated.
Because: it's not dificult to find dracula.. it would've been one of the most fun parts, but there are so many event cards that simple tell you where he is.. so instead of hunting him down, you simply have to trot after him & make sure he didn't drop any vampires while stacking up tons of weapons to finally attack & slay him.

That alone takes a lot of time, time both parties have to invest.. and the other thing is, half of the other event cards are cards that either do or cancel effects from the opponent.. so you constantly play cards that reverse each other.. feels like your Sisyphos.
All of that results in games that are incredibly long (we're talking 5-6 hours) and more often than not, come down to lucky die-rolls.
Tried to fix the game with house rules but i gave up.

___________________________
Love the theme, the 1 vs. many. the hide & seek, the fights in between, the traps dracula lays, the fact that in this rather long game there is no player elemination.. love the game.

Hm.. i have to say it's getting a bit samey recently.. there is a pretty clear strategy dracula & the hunters have to follow. Maybe i should try playing one of the hunters for a change. Droped from 9 to 8. But still a very good game.

RATING: 7
Unusual deduction/combat game with many possibilities. Unlike anything I've ever played. Fighting is thematic, almost cinematic, but that can actually get tiresome after awhile. Game usually drags on too long.

Addenda: Each time I play this game, my rating goes down another point. Too long and frustrating what with the "Dracula Wins" card (Evasion). That card exists, apparently, only to keep Hunters from drawing event cards -- but they need to draw events to have a hope of countering it. It wouldn't be so bad if Dracula won instantly, but the teleport across Europe means the Hunters have to continue trying to hopelessly hunt him down for an hour more of painful, pointless boredom.

I've had to delete all "teleport" text from my game to make it enjoyable. Changing the Evasion card by deleting the middle sentence makes this game truly an enjoyable experience. Short and sweet, not too long and frustrating!

No Teleportation without Representation!

RATING: 2
(copy and pasted from my comment on 3rd edition, as the differences between all the editions do not impact the core issues I have with this game)

You could not design a game less for me than this one if you tried to. I think the biggest problem for me is that I do not find the core puzzle of deducing where Dracula could be engaging at all. Perhaps if it was contained within a game that was not seemingly designed to last forever, it might hold my interest longer, but as it is, it seems that skillful and/or lucky play by Dracula results in a game where *nothing happens* for hours. For at least 2 of the 3 times I've played this, we've called the game at the 3 hour mark when it was clear that we had at least 1-2 more hours remaining.

I do have to give this game credit for something though. It's the perfect illustration to me that what constitutes good game design is ultimately a subjective thing, as lots of people, including friends of mine, clearly love to play this game and it's unlikely they are all pretending to like it just to mess with me. :-D

RATING: 7
Good deduction game with great theme.  I find myself more and more leaning towards Amerithrash games, as they are much more fun to play.  Initially, I was afraid that FoD will be entertaining only for the Dracula player, but fortunately the Hunters also have a great time.  It is just a different experience and an advantage of this game.  It is as if you got two games in one, which is a bonus.

My greatest concern was the play time.  The game is quite long ( 2 hours), but the time flies, especially when the Hunters are on the Dracula's trail and keep close behind.  You can feel the tension!  The only negative feeling you (Hunters) get is when Dracula escapes a long-woven net and you have to start over.  It may be depressing!

1.09.2007 - painted the figures.  Finally, I do not confuse them on the board!

23.01.2008 - Traded for BattleLore+Call to Arms.  Could not miss such an opportunity.  I still like Fury of Dracula though.

RATING: 8
It's distinctly a Fantasy Flight game, with tons of little fiddly bits that make it a hair more complex than it needs to be. It's also distinctly a game that a group needs to build its evening around--with a skilled Dracula player, the game takes every bit of the 3-hour expected playtime, and you need a group prepared for that investment. It's very pretty and atmospheric, the design is quite solid, and the hidden movement, cat-and-mouse dynamic is a fun mechanic no other game I've played has really replicated. Combat is not great, though; the newer edition does that a little better, and I suggest house-ruling to streamline it.

RATING: 9
Owned SINCE 2012
I play this game with my family (wife and kids 7- 11 years old) and we like it. It does a great job capturing the feel and theme of hunting Dracula in old Europe. This game is definitively a deduction game first, and fighting game second; which is perfect, and just what I wanted. I would love to rate this 9, but the fighting mechanic seems a little ruff, and takes some getting use to.   
  UPDATE- After more plays the fighting mechanics do flow better, but something else, something easier, probably could of been used instead. I noticed that some games are very suspenseful and tense, with everything hanging on a single move or roll of the dice. Those are games that deserve a "10" rating. Other games are boring, and those can be rated a "5". I think this is because players have a lot of choices, and depending on what they do it can lead to a great, close game or a game where there is little action or a clear winner from the beginning. I am glad I have this game, maybe a little overpriced for what it does, but it fills a unique gaming experience and does it well. I can not see any other deduction game being better. We just played another great game yesterday (before this edit), one where everything depended on a single battle and everyone was watching. Even people who had not played were in suspense because of the situation.. Yeah, when this game is good it is just great.

RATING: 7.5
This is a great change from Euro-gaming which I have done so much of lately. The theme is so well implimented and production values are pretty good too except for the cards which could have been thicker. 

[u]Pros:[/u] Strong theme, very unique, intriguing, fun, nice bits, scales 2 to 5(see comments below however), some tension, neat mechanics  

[u]Cons:[/u] Slightly long, can be slightly mechanical at times when either chasing Drac or playing Drac and just running away, slightly lower strategic level of play (its there but more for Drac than the hunters IMO), downtime with more than 3 players

[u]Summary:[/u] Overall a great game and very welcomed addition to my collection. After playing with 5 people I can tell you that to enjoy this you need 5 VERY PATIENT people, 4 would not be too great either, too much downtime. Best with either 2 or 3 people total IMO and NOT a gamers game or for anyone on a strict Euro diet. 

[u]UPDATE:[/u] 8 => 7.5 Scaling issue keeps it from hitting the table

RATING: 6
February 2011

Initial Rating: 7.0 (February 2011)

It has a huge manual and, thus far, I have been unable to play as Dracula. Still I like the game but I prefer to play it with 3 players, 4 tops. More than that and the down time can be an issue.

Dracula is extremely powerful at night, but ridiculously weak during the day so during the day Dracula has to hide and the hunters need to deduce his whereabouts, at night it is the hunters who need to thread carefully as Dracula can unleash a set of powerful attacks, nonetheless, I find the game relies heavily on the ability of the Dracula player to evade the hunters, if they can´t catch him Dracula has won.

Fury of Dracula has a strong theme and it is pretty easy to learn, the play time hoovers around the 3 hour mark. I really enjoy the game but it is a game I would like to play once a month, more than that and the game can lose its appeal.

Current Rating: 7.5

RATING: 8.5
This is a very fun game that is fun for both hunters and Dracula. There is considerable strategic depth and the game is high on theme. It's very easy to "get into it" once you start playing and are hoping to keep running or sneak up on those pesky hunters or are hoping to stake Dracula to the wall.

It does have a steep learning curve but once you play through it a little, it seems to have an intuitive set of rules.

I recommend this one highly.

RATING: 6
I have had a lot of fun with this game in the past. The combat system is very clever, I love it. I enjoyed the game as a unique and thematic experience. However, these days I find it lacking in several key areas, and that keeps it from being played. 

The main issue is inconsistent tension. The hunters don't know how close they are to finding Dracula. For them there is a lot of somewhat boring casting of the net which hopefully results in pinpointing Dracula. The experience of the Dracula player is great, it's very tense to watch the hunters plan out their moves.

The game is also quite long for what it offers strategically. For hidden movement I'd rather break out Scotland Yard.

RATING: 8.5
WOW!  Grasping this game on your first play is a chore.  FoD itself isn't overly complicated, but there such a large meta-game to learn since there are many special abilities to understand on item and event cards. FoD is an excellent blend of theme, deduction, cooperation, light RPG, and direct confrontation; additionally the production values of the FF version were top notch.  And since it's assymetrical, if you ever get bored, you can play the other side to spice it up.  Dracula is constantly on the move from one city to the next.  This is simulated by him pulling a card from a site deck and placing it face down on a track in front of him (along with one of his minions). As you move your Hunters across the board, hoping to land on a city which is in Dracula's face down track so you can uncover the card and begin deducting where he is, you gather items and event cards to help you cope with Dracula.  Be wary, as Dracula isn't the only creature out for you, you'll have to deal with his minions if you uncover his trail...and sometimes it's more important to deal with them as it is Dracula because if the minion is a vampire and left to mature too long (Dracula's trail is only so long, and eventually the cards start falling off the end of the track), Dracula gets big points (2 of the 6 needed).  But the weapon items that hurt the minions may not necessarily hurt Dracula;  Have you balanced your character well enough to handle the task?  If you're not prepared, and Dracula takes your hunter out, 2 more points for him (but don't worry, your hunter isn't permanently dead, just reset).  Not to mention, every round moves to time of day marker, 3 of which are day and 3 night.  Once a day night cycle is complete, Dracula gets a point.  Guess who's stronger at night?  That's right, Dracula.  How desparate are you to fight him then?  Is it down to the wire?  Have you prepared your hunters for the task and coordinated well enough with your partner(s)?  

Due to it's many characteristics and depth, I think I will be interested in this game for some time to come...rating likely to go up.


The main detractor of this game is the randomness of the die rolls.  I plan on implementing a system similar to Knizia's Lord of the Rings: The Confrontation using only cards.  Check the Variants section of the Forum: http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/106224
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
Some games are all about the theme and this is one of them. The immersion is great, keeping in mind that you know in advance that being Dracula is all about hiding and not biting and killing. Personally, I find it ok, as the seek & destroy Dracula is more from the new books and films: in the old ones, it was a perverse and sneaky creature that wrecked evil everywhere he go.

So, what does this offer? Mainly, theme and fun, but also the deduction mechanism is particularly well implemented. All in all, this is an excellent game for rolegamers, fans of the ameritrash thing and fans of gothic literature (did I mention that the theme in this one is great?). Also, the components are top notch.

You always play with four hunters and, obviously, one Dracula. This seems like a great setup for five players, but that's not how this game rolls. Playing as Dracula is always fun and challenging, no matter the number of players. But hunters? In every game I've played there has always been at least one hunter pawn who hasn't been involved in the game at all. If you have less players than hunter pieces, the less useful pawn can be left aside, with players agreeing in what to do with it, while each player gets its own hunter to focus on. But if hunter piece is controlled by an individual player, well, said lonesome hunter isn't going to have much fun. With two players the issue is the total opposite: whoever is playing the four hunters suffers an information overdose. Not boring, but not optimal.

One more thing: if all the hunters are new to the game, make sure to warn them about the advantages of spamming the event deck or, most likely, they won't know where Dracula is most of the time and will get bored (oh, and mentioning that one event is a "Scotty, teleport Dracula" is also important to avoid unexpected frustration).

RATING: 8
From what i've read: Typical Fantasy Flight game. Lot's of flavor but very little game. Move peon. Draw event. Move peon. Roll die. Move. Roll....... 

from a review:

"Another thing that irks me about Fury of Dracula is combat/event cards. All too often I have played games in which the Dracula player was playing an extremely smart, well thought out game that was obliterated because the Hunter’s got lucky die rolls or drew all the right event cards. This, again, works both ways.

These reasons are why I call Fury of Dracula my groups “cult classic”. Just like Lucio Fulci films, the game has its flaws. If you take it too seriously you’ll end up with a few players that had a great time and a few that end the night pissed off and discouraged. But, like Fulci films, if you play the game with the right amount of players (3-4) and you all have the right mindset, Fury of Dracula can be a great time for all. As long as these conditions are met, I recommend this game wholeheartedly."

RATING: N/A
In this game of Gothic adventure, one player takes the role of Dracula while up to four others attempt to stop him by controlling Vampire hunters from the famous Bram Stoker novel.

Dracula has returned, and is determined to control all of Europe by creating an undead empire of Vampires. Dracula uses a deck of location cards to secretly travel through Europe, leaving a trail of encounters and events for the hunters that chase him.

Meanwhile, the hunters attempt to track and destroy Dracula using the limited information available to them - a task easier said than done when their prey has the power to change forms into a wolf or bat, and can even melt away into the mist when confronted.

Better deduction game then Letters of White chapel and Scotland yard in my opinion as there is a better theme, and player interaction (attacking).

RATING: 7.5
Thematic, semi-cooperative, deduction/search game. Players play either Dracula or one of four Hunters. Dracula tries to hide at day times, attack at nights, gain power with each night-day turn and with each successfully placed vampire. The Hunters, on the other hand, try to find, catch and destroy Dracula. The twist is that Dracula moves secretly around Europe.
The game is fun, very thematic and also luck driven - some event cards are very powerful, but the luck seems to balance out evenly. It's a good experience game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
[microbadge=419][microbadge=5792][microbadge=2135]

One of my favorite AT titles.  Good fun and balance as either Dracula or as a Hunter.  There are so many little details I love in this game.  The location deck is inspired.  Drawing events from the bottom to hide card backs is great (and even having events from both factions in the same deck is great).  The train die is fun.  The combat system is fantastic: you get a wonderfully realistic narrative since successful attacks change their effects based not only on what the attack was but also what the opponent's attempted attack was.  I'm always down for a game of Fury, on either side of the board.

RATING: 6
[Played 22 times]

"Debugged" version of the original (no more player elimination, more balanced cards, new movement rules for Dracula raising interaction and deduction, Dracula must play an encounter every turn).
Luck is still very important (dice and cards), but a bit less than before.
Atmosphere has been preserved.
Cooperation (with more than two players) and a bit of deduction embellish the game.
Probably better with fewer players (brisker pace).
It still has its flaws (FFG rushed development shows once more).

Playing with all experienced players makes the game both shorter and more interesting (even if it feels biased towards the Hunters, the hints given in the rulebook and some house rules should help).

Some components (character sheets, box insert, lack of a cards/tiles holder) are disappointing given the price tag.

RATING: N/A
In this game of Gothic adventure, one player takes the role of Dracula while up to four others attempt to stop him by controlling Vampire hunters from the famous Bram Stoker novel.
Dracula has returned, and is determined to control all of Europe by creating an undead empire of Vampires. Dracula uses a deck of location cards to secretly travel through Europe, leaving a trail of encounters and events for the hunters that chase him.
Meanwhile, the hunters attempt to track and destroy Dracula using the limited information available to them - a task easier said than done when their prey has the power to change forms into a wolf or bat, and can even melt away into the mist when confronted.
To save Europe and rid the world of Dracula's foul plague, the hunters must destroy Dracula before he earns enough victory points to win the game... will they have enough wit and bravery to defeat the dark count?
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
2.9 I've changed my mind on this game. I didnt like it in the first couple of games. There is a big rules overhead to playing the game, particularly if you are playing Dracula. There's a lot to get the hang of - the cards, the weapons, the fight system itself. The game will reward you the more you play.

You must sit down and read the rules before you start, and not try and quick start the game (like I did with some friends).

The pieces are nice quality. A dracula 'screen' would have been a nice addition - I have to play Dracula from inside the lid to stop people seeing my cards.

Its worth reading the quick start guide and rules addendums from BGG before you start playing as well, as they cover a number of the major points of confusion.

The game can get bogged down in analysis paralysis (but at least the team can talk to each other), and I've never had a short game of Dracula - it can take 4 or so hours.

I think if you enjoy the cerebral experience of the cat and mouse chase, you will like this game. There's not really another game like it (apart from Scotland Yard or Letters from Whitechapel).

Bought on ebay, imported in from Australia. Later replaced with a second copy when the first got beer flooded by Matt G.

Chit pull, partnerships, point to point movement, secret unit deployment, variable player powers.

To sleeve. Have sleeves.

Might get replaced with Specter Ops.

RATING: 10
Fury of Dracula is a near perfect game in my opinion. It is tense and exciting, simple to teach yet deep in game play, both tactical and strategic and is one of the most thematic games you can play. It is equally challenging for both the hunters and Dracula and the game play is varied enough to warrant many repeated playings. The game flows like a great horror story with each turn like another chapter in a late-night page turner that you can't put down.

I ALWAYS am enthusiastic to play this and will seldom turn down a game.

RATING: 9.5
Fury of Dracula is an investment, plain and simple. You could, I suppose, pick this off the shelf one evening (e.g. Halloween) and give it a go the same night. But, I would argue that it is important for someone in the group to have either played the game before, or at the very least, have someone who has a solid grasp of the rules. Because the rules in this game are complex, perhaps overly-complex. I understand that the designer might have found that certain rule exceptions were necessary after feedback from play testing. I'm sure they all serve to balance the game properly. Though, despite that hard work, I find that this game, without any modifications and all players being equal, favors Dracula quite a bit. Nevertheless, my wife and I spent the better part of 3 hours getting through the 30 page rulebook. Even after a close read, and relatively quick play (considering it was our first game, of course), our first game took over 5 hours! The Hunters ended up defeating Dracula in the small hours of the final day. This first game was fun, but it was WAY TOO LONG! There's just not enough game here, in my opinion, to take more than 4 hours, let alone 5. In our second game, we made some fairly basic modifications to shorten the game. We also kept balance in mind. If we simply shortened the game and did nothing else, Dracula would have a significant advantage. So, we made a couple of other tweaks as well. Our second game took only 2 hours, with quick play. I wanted to share our house rules with those who simply can't set aside a whole afternoon or evening to play this game. 

Changes: 
-Place the vampire marker on the "2" space of the vampire track. (This is the most basic way to shorten the game).
-Remove 5 blood points from Dracula's play sheet. He should start with 10 instead of 15. 
-Reduce the Godalming's health by 4, Helsing's by 3, and reduce Harker and Seward by 2.  
-After the first day, hunters receive 2 resolve per day rather than 1. 

*Keep in mind that we wanted to make the fewest amount of changes necessary in order to: 
1.shorten the game 
2. maintain balance 
3.In the case of the hunters, hopefully improve their odds of winning, though only slightly. 

I'm sure that hundreds of people have bought or traded for Fury of Dracula and have never completed a game. Beyond that, I'm sure that many have looked at the rulebook in awe and have never even attempted a playthrough. Some gamers simply don't have a a whole afternoon to play a game, and if they do, they only do once or twice a year. Shortening the game to 2 hours makes it much more feasible to get to the table, and much more enjoyable for the hunters, in my opinion. I'm sharing this information, not because I think the designer got it wrong, but because I want as many people as possible to enjoy this game. We absolutely love it, and I hope others that are hesitant to pull it off the shelf, realize that this is a game that can be played in a reasonable amount of time. More importantly, Fury of Dracula is an amazing experience!

Update 8/30/15:

Finally got the chance to play this with 3. It's much less housekeeping at this number. I enjoyed it quite a bit. The two other players felt a little powerless at times, since they couldn't seem to catch up to me until the end of the game. But, I still think it's tremendous.

RATING: 9
Comment after a single play. Game lasted a little long (6 hours!) But it was incredibly tense right up to the very end. 

Houserules for next game: 1 blood loss for sea is automatic. Time still moves when Dracula is at sea. The hunters' sea ally makes Dracula lose 1 extra blood when he first goes into sea.

Night: Dracula can lose 1 blood to reroll a dice in combat

Castle Dracula: While here, you must stay until the end of the game. Dracula instantly heals up to 6 total blood (if he was under).
You gain 1 blood each turn and can place an encounter instead of a movement card. Castle Dracula can get multiple encounters on it (only 1 new vampire). Cards and encounters still shift off the trail each turn.

Event Setup - 1 Evasion and 1 Hypnosis are shuffled into the last half of the deck.
