I suspect that the rating for this will go up with more plays, as long as I don't get too annoyed with battle mechanism.  I'm probably more schizophrenic about this game than any other: there are things about it that I find toweringly awesome and things I detest.  It's the only game I've played that makes me want to read the book on which it is based.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
La Furia de Drácula... Menos mal que no me lo compré hace 4 años por E-bay. Un día, comprando minis por E-bay, vi que un tio vendía la versión antigua de Games Workshop por 30 euros y me llamó la atención el juego. Busqué información en la web de la BGG y estuve a muy poco de comprárselo. Al final me echaé atrás porque me dió la sensación de que era muy dependiente del idioma (inglés). Aún así me quedé con la mosca detrás de la oreja (a mi la temática de vampiros clásicos me encanta). 2 años más tarde, buscando noticas para una revista de juegos me entero que FFG lo iba a reeditar, al igual que estaba haciendo con el Arkham Horror de Chaosium. Fue entonces cuando el sector de los juegos de mesa en España empezó a despegar como ahora. Edge y Devir sacaban casi bimensualmente algún juego traducido y pensé que quizá tocara la campana. Y al final ha tocado... Y todo esto viene a que menos mal que no me lo pillé en su momento en inglés porque, en efecto, el juego tiene muchas cartas con textos bastante extensos... más de lo que me pensaba. Y el juego no es sencillo. Para nada.

Vamos a necesitar una media hora para explicaros todas las reglas, más o menos como en el Arkham Horror. Además, también requiere que los jugadores se vayan leyendo detenidamente sus cartas durante el juego, porque hay algunas con efectos y textos extensos.... Pero el juego tiene una pinta estupenda. Creo que retrata muy bien la atmósfera del vampiro. Los jugadores tienen que compenetrarse muy bien entre sí para acabar con el jugador que lleva a Drácula y eso, es más dificil de lo que en un principio pueda parecer. Además visualmente el juego es una preciosidad. El tablero, que muestra un mapa de la Europa de finales del siglo XIX es bonito de cojones. Viene con unas minis, pero, aunque no están mal, son de plástico y vienen algo dobladas.

Puntos fuertes: al igual que el Arkham Horror, es un juego muy rejugable porque hay una gran cantidad y variedad de cartas que hace difícil que una partida sea igual que la otra. Las estrategias son muchas y el factor colaborativo es determinante. También es importante la persona que desempeña el papel de Drácula, ya que debe manejar bien las habilidades y poderes del vampiro para no caer facilmente en la trampa de los otros jugadores. Eso determinará si la partida dura 2 horas o 3. Casi ná.

Lecturas recomendadas:
"Drácula", de Bram Stoker. Para quien no se la haya leído se lo recomiendo encarecidamente. No es solo la NOVELA de vampiros por excelencia y fuente de toda inspiración, sino que su estilo narrativo es muy original (sobre todo teniendo en cuenta la fecha en que se escribió) ya que algunos capítulos funcionan perfectamente siendo simplemente las cartas y correspondencia que mantienen los protagonistas con sus particulares puntos de vista en la trama.

"La historiadora", de Elizabeth Kostova. Este tochazo de libro tuve oportunidad de leerlo hace 1 año. Aunque ha sido un best seller, a mí personalmente no me convenció. La trama tarda muchísimo en arrancar y muchos pasajes están extremadamente forzados. Pero aún así, es una interesante novela que narra la investigación durante años de una familia por descubrir y matar de una vez por todas a Drácula en plena Guerra Fría.

Fury of Dracula is a solid game with bleeding great components.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Played once, as Dracula.  This is an amazingly well-themed game wherein one to four players team up as "hunters" who are scouring Europe to find (and kill) Dracula, who is always played by a single player.  This is, at its heart, a deduction game - Dracula moves in secret, but leaves a trail behind.  Anytime a hunter come across Dracula's trail, Dracula reveals that he was there (and how many turns ago he was there).  There's a ton of cards that can come into play, and these all add a delicious element of rnadomness that turns the game into an adventure: both Dracula and the Hunters must use lots of logic to figure out where to go (Dracula must figure out where the Hunters are likely to go, and the Hunters must figure out Dracula's likely moves).  Then, once the parties meet, battles ensue.

Printout out player aids is ESSENTIAL for this game.  Printing out the inverse-map for Dracula is key (as is building a shield for Dracula and giving Dracula colored cubes to track his past and present locations).  Also key is to print out the giant tables of the results of all possible battle combinations - this grid looks imposing at first, but is key to choosing well in a battle.  Also helpful are turn-summaries.

This game is LONG - it took an hour or more for rules, and at least four hours to play.  But those four hours were extremely fun-filled hours - Dracula (me) was having a great time (even when I was almost dead), and the four Hunters were also having a great time.  Helping mitigate the length is that the hunters are nearly constantly involved in logical deducation, in which all the players must work together to figure out the logic trees (so you're never waiting for someone else's turn).  And, after every move a new piece of information about Dracula's trail is revealed, starting the logic all over again.  

If you've got the right group, this is an insanely fun game.  I loved it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
In Fury of Dracula, one player plays the role of the nefarious monster while four others play the hunters chasing him across Europe. Dracula moves secretly with his set of cards which is placed down turn after turn, leaving nasty traps and surprises for hunters who follow. Hunters must deduce and try to find Dracula and ultimately try and kill him.

This game is a fun deduction game that has players guessing where Dracula is on a map.  Both the hunters and Dracula have their own set of cards that they can play at certain times. Although the game play itself is simple the details of the game is quite complex. There are lots of rules and exceptions on when certain actions can be taken; certain cards can be played, the various effects of different actions, special abilities, etc… It can be quite over-whelming for a first time player. However, if you’re up for the challenge you’ll find Fury of Dracula to be an intense game of cat-and-mouse.

RATING: 7
The comparison with Scotland Yard is inevitable but this game has a lot more going on. I liked it but you do need to have sufficient time set aside to play it. If I want something lighter and reasonably quick I'd pick Scotland Yard but if I had the time I'd pick this one first.

The hunters all have special abilities which seem to suggest certain roles, Van Helsing can survive more bites so should fight Dracula, Lord Godalming is tough when taking on minions so should clean those out to stop them maturing, Mina can get cards and swap them. However all of that is not easy to engine when you've got no idea of where Drac is and little idea of where he's been. It's like the designers came up with these roles for the characters without thinking how the characters were going to implement those roles.

RATING: 6
A fairly good game of cat and mouse, Fury of Dracula can be a lot of fun at times, other games it just sucks.

I love the theme and its an exciting idea, its just that the game encourages Dracula to be less fury and more a little sissy running for all his life.

This is because combat comes down to the roll of a D6, and with a bad couple of rolls Dracula can be killed outright in under a minute. This encourages a cowardly style of play in which Dracula should avoid fighting at all costs, something which just seems to go against the overall theme and if done successfully can draw out the game for longer then its worth.

Shame because otherwise I really feel this is something I could have sunk my teeth into. Sadly the more I play it the less I like it.

Fury of Dracula 3rd Edition has several improvements and is vastly better then this version- I'd get it over 2nd edition any day!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Up to four players try to find another player controlling Dracula who is secretly moving around in Europe. However, the hunters can stumble on Dracula's trail, or use special event cards to find his exact location. The hunters must kill Dracula in combat to win. There is a night and day aspect as well, where Dracula is stronger at night. Dracula's movement over Europe is tracked with cards on a sliding 7 card track, which means Dracula cannot visit a city twice within 7 turns. Special event cards allow Dracula or the hunters to break rules of the game or gain special advantages. 

It's an okay thematic update to Scotland Yard, but it plays longer, around two and half to three hours. Fun to play to experience the theme, especially if you have read the novels and are familiar with the characters.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Looks great, made by Fantasy Flight, good reviews; only problem is that I already have Scotland Yard and like it a lot which has the disadvantage of not being as deep or as long but also has the advantage of being not as deep or as long. Focusing on just the catching and finding makes the game quick, purely skill based (except starting location) and streamlined. I'm worried that by adding this RP game on top of something like Scotland Yard, it may drag it out too much and de emphasize the finding too much. Though it still overall looks great and if I saw a great deal on it, I would buy it.

RATING: 7
Scotland Yard with vampires, done up with beautiful FFG chrome and lotsa bits.  What's not to love?

Well, assuming competent players on all sides, the outta-box game is nearly impossible for Dracula to win.  Everything weighs for the Hunters.  Daytime combat is absolutely predictable.  Still very fun, but also fatalistic.  I can also see this game working well with a parent vs. a bunch of 10-year-olds, teaching them basic deduction skills and whatnot, as long as the parent is Drac at first.

That said, a few rules tweaks help clear up lingering issues and FFG gives suggestions on how to even things out... even if, for some reason, the Hunters feel outgunned and outnumbered.  (My favorite variant is FFG's Republic of Rome-style variant, where only one Hunter can emerge victorious.)

RATING: 7.3
Deduction game that pits 4 players (Hunters) against another player (Dracula). It has some other mechanics, but the best part is the deduction of Dracula's moving path, as well as Dracula bluffing and dodging skills.

The theme is really well integrated. All the cards reflect some aspect of the novel and it really puts you in the skins of the characters.

The components and graphic aspect is very nice (a bit "old style", reflecting the gothic nature of the story). I like the map, but I would have preferred it to be a bit bigger (even if I don't like unnecesarily big maps).

Maybe the game is too lucky, not only in the combat (Rock, Paper, Scissors + dice), but also in the event cards. There are some ones that are very powerful and can be game changing depending in the moment you get them.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
That's what you would get by crossing Scotland Yard with Arkham Horror. Awesome game! FoD has been on my monitor since about the birth of Christ, but had too many doubts about its quality, and the friends was totally indifferent about the game. Can't even remember having ever discussed the game outside the internet. Well, that's too bad, because in order to make it short: I Love Fury of Dracula !!!

Four hours flew by, I almost missed the last train, although unfortunately, we still couldn't get the game finished. But anyway, great game! ... At least if you have the time for it and if you think it's more fun to kill the old Count and his minions, rather than to catch Mister X or Jack the Ripper. Unlike Scotland Yard and Whitechapel, Fury of Dracula is a cat-and-mouse game where the roles can change suddenly. Sometimes, it isn't quite clear who's actually the mouse and who's the cat. The tension, the atmosphere - it all seems just right! Possibly an effect of its semi-cooperative nature?  I like teams games a lot, you see. I've briefly considered, but in a rush I can't think of a team game that I did not like. Malefiz, Scotland Yard, Descent, Battlestar Galactica ... even Canasta that I still enjoy playing with the family ,

One thing is certain: Fury of Dracula will come onto my shelf, though probably as the current 3rd edition, first of all because 2nd is hard to get, and second, because of some improvements the 3rd edition is said to have according to my trusted geekbuddies.

RATING: 9
There was a lot of discussion on Fury on BoardGameGeek when it was first released. I was starting to look at co-operative or semi-coop and it looked good.

It has been a 'steady' game for us, making it to the table every 6-8 weeks.

Dripping with theme. It plays very well, though needs an experienced player to take on the lead role. We also find it good when we have a newcomer (can easily slot into the hunter team and picked up the game) or when someone if coming a little late (we can start and they can take over their character partway through)

We play 5 handed - or 6 handed with the 'Dracula's Minion' option off BGG.

3/2010 - updated rating from 8.25 to 9. Gets better with every playing, even after 5 years. In constant demand in the gaming group. The subtlety and variations (ie replayability) shine through over time.

RATING: 4
The upgraded version still sees Dracula moving secretly, being chased between the cities of Europe by three detectives. It's a harder deduction than Scotland Yard by allowing only three detectives, and made harder by allowing Dracula to stay still and, if he moves, to offer no clues. If you do land on him, you have to defeat him in combat to win. And if you don't kill Dracula, allow him to escape with no clues as to which direction. Oh, and if Dracula reaches a port, he can travel via sea to any other port, leaving no clues as to where, meaning you have to start all over again. A pretty frustrating par for the course. It just seemed too much like wandering in the dark, not much deductive work, and then succumb to the luck of the events and the combat. Bearable if you're entranced by the theme.

RATING: 8
The theme has been adapted brilliantly, second only to the war of the ring! I like the game system, a more sophisticated system than Scotland Yard's, but also more random elements that can drag things down a bit. In the whole a fantastic game though, great fun and interactivity! Should just play in slightly less time to my mind. And also!! Must be played with 5 players! It still works with 4 but less then this is not so fun anymore, and it's best playing with a clever Dracula player!

After giving the third edition a go, I am pleased to own the second version instead. The length of the game has not been significantly improved. I prefer the components of the second edition (specially Drac's encounter tiles are nicer), has got more space around the board for the players, and the combat system never really bothered me much. Also, a big deal is that the Hunters seem to be able to initiate a fight only at night whereas Dracula only at day, to me this is a big deal since it will make Dracula's attempt to fight the hunters less likely than in the second edition where it might be risked in an attempt to win the game by the Dracula player... it's the same game, and the differences are not significant and some of them actually make the game more fiddly (train booking, encounter cards, etc.)

- The rule book is not so super. Great design, yes, but somewhat clumsy. It's difficult to find specific details when you need to check.

[b]Strong theme[/b]

RATING: 7
Un gioco appassionante, con atmosfera, ambientazione e veste grafica di altissimo livello. L'esperienza di gioco è appagante, sia per i Cacciatori che deducono, si organizzano e si aiutano che per Dracula, che gode quando i primi sono totalmente fuori strada e se la fa sotto quando gli sono a un tiro di schioppo. Mai vista così tanta immedesimazione col proprio personaggio da parte di persone a digiuno di boardgame e giochi di ruolo. Un bel cooperativo estremamente calato nell'ambientazione, con un paio di difetti: si passa l'80% del gioco a stanare il Vampiro in una divertente gara di deduzione, ma il duello - uno dei pilastri del gioco - è assolutamente dimenticabile; inoltre, l'enormità di eccezioni, carte evento e casi particolari spezzetta alcune fasi del gioco e obbliga chi non gioca frequentemente a giocare con le regole a portata di mano. Rimane un bel gioco, che purtroppo non può essere proposto spesso a causa della lunga durata di una partita (e un setup molto lungo).

RATING: 6
An odd game.  Scotland Yard with fighting and additional victory conditions.  Have only played as a hunter, and the game has a tremendous ebb and flow to it.  Some rounds are really fun - when you're hot on Dracula's trail, when you have a tremendous amount of weapons and are ready to kick butt, etc.  Other rounds, when you have a general idea where Dracula is but aren't exactly on his trail, when you have all the cards you need, etc., are really boring, and recall fruitless rounds of Talisman, when you draw useless cards and your character is kind of tough, but not tough enough to try to win.

That is, the game is really fun or tense about 2/3 of the time, but the other 1/3 is kind of boring.  If it were always like the fun/tense 2/3, I'd give the game a 9, because it's really fun, even when Dracula is kicking your ass at midnight in London.

UPDATE:  Man, this game brings out the worst in me. The power of the cards are too all over the place, leading to some frustrating plays.  Also, the combat is a glorified "who can roll higher" thing, which isn't all that great.  I have to knock it down a notch.

RATING: 9
OWN: 2ND & 3RD EDITIONS

Original comments based on 2nd Edition...

Great integration of theme and plenty of depth. Very clever cards allow for hidden movement of Dracula and clues are gradually revealed to the hunters.

Plays well with only 2 players, although the hunters can be quite an effort for one person (managing all the cards and abilities effectively enough to keep up with Dracula).

If only the game could run a little shorter (maybe with more experience). Scotland Yard makes for a much lighter & quicker alternative, but Garibaldi: La Trafila gets my vote over either - it plays almost as quickly as Scotland Yard with much of the depth of FoD.

WARNING: Rules are lengthier than needed, and poorly organised.

RATING: 1
FOD was a dud as far as I'm concerned. I'm surprised considering I loved Scotland Yard and I played it only several years ago. I don't mind the cat and mouse chase, that's part of the fun (usually). However, combat leaves a lot to be desired. There is no drama just a bunch of stupid dice rolling and cards that leave you with a frustrated feeling. It's hard to spend four hours on a game, most of it just moving around a board to finally corner Dracula (by sheer luck on top of it because we had one card that allowed it) and then storm him with three out of four hunters only to get your ass handed to you. I play board games for three reasons off the top of my head. Number one for fun. Number two for the social aspect. Number three for a challenge. Fun factor was in the negatives, social time is there in most games, this one too, challenge was so so. This won't be getting another play from me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This game would be much better if two things changed.  One, it needs to be shorter, it takes entirely too long to play this game.  However, the game itself is interesting enough that I would overlook that if only...

The combat system needs to suck less.  I'm fine with dice rolling.  What I'm not fine with is ludicrously random dice rolls.  Rolling a single D6 against another is just dumb.  There are ways to do dice rolling so that it doesn't depend so heavily on luck.  Arkham Horror rolls multiple dice for hits, Risk rolls multiple dice and matches up highest rolls.

This would be a great game if only the combat wasn't so flawed.  I would be hard-pressed to play this game again without some variant which changed combat.  Perhaps rolling two dice and taking the average.

RATING: 9
I love the cat-and-mouse aspect of this game.  I love that drac is SOMEWHERE on that board, you just don't know where.  I love the asymmetric strategies that hunters and drac have to use.  The game "looks" great, and the theme is top notch (it even made me want to read the novel!).  I would try to get as many players as possible.  While it can be played by two players, the hunter player has quite a bit of work managing all four characters (and their events, items, movement, etc).  Also, combat is relatively infrequent, so if you're looking for a combat-oriented game this isn't it.  Although I don't like that combat is based on a single die roll, I do like the roll that the combat cards play in creating a realistic atmosphere.

RATING: 7.1
Only played once.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Pros:
1. The Chase - Hunting down Dracula is a blast. Wandering around Europe and stumbling upon Dracula's trail, then trying to work out where he must be is by far the best part of this game.
2. Risky Decisions - During the chase portion of the game, you have to decide do I get items or do I move. It's risky to try and supply at night because you may help dracula. I enjoyed the drama this little, but important decision added to the game.

Cons:
1. Battle System - This is likely the worst battle system I've ever played in a game. Flip a card, check if icons match. Majority of the time, the icons do not match. So, there's a lot of flipping, with nothing happening. Boring.
2. Items - You make risky decisions to potentially add items to use in battle. Then, you use the item once in a battle, the icons usually don't match, then it's discarded. It's hard to see why you should ever bother collecting items. 
3. Dracula Powerful in Battle - Dracula's battle cards are very powerful. Making the battle system infuriating. Not only is random chance that you'll do damage, you're also dealing with ridiculously powerful cards.
4. Length of the game - The game is just generally too long. It's a 2.5 to 3 hour game. The fun portion of the game which is the chase only takes up about an hour. The last 2 hours is just fighting dracula, you lose, he moves, you move to the next city he must be at, you fight, you lose, he move..... rinse and repeat. No drama, nothing to really change it up.

Summary: This game needs a third edition where the emphasis is put on the chase. Or they need some way to make the battles more interesting. The battle portion of the game is boring and repetitive. There's a minimal chance I will ever play this game again.

RATING: 4
This should NOT be recommended for newer gamers.

Shockingly unbalanced gameplay, and the overpowering event cards make a mockery of what (IMO) should be a deduction, thief/hunter game. If 3 hours of cat and mouse, decided by "who has the right event card" is your idea of fun, then you'll like this game.

It's the kind of game where if you had the time and patience to invest in playing it enough, it would reward you with better gameplay, and the theme is very nice. [i]My rating of 4 is targetted to the first plays.[/i] Afterwards, I could see it rising to as much as 7.

RATING: 7
Fury's ratings keep rising with repeat playing.But when I first played, gameplay was slow and repetative with too many event and item cards thrown around. Not enough for the hunters to do except bide their time sorting through the items deck for decent weapons. With four players I just wanted Dracula to be caught and have that stake plunged into his heart as play clicked well over the 90 min mark - and I was Dracula! 

Then I played three players (players controlled two hunters each), and it was far better, even with the odd lull in play. Lots to do, there's always one hunter close to Dracula and the event cards gives each game a different spin. It's even better playing as Dracula! Tense, and dripping with theme.

I'd almost refuse to play this with three - four hunter players, but it's a great three player game (two players may mean too much for the hunter to handle), especially if everyone plays fast and knows the rules.

RATING: 7
Few games dig as deep into their themes as this one. If you appreciated Coppola's "Dracula" movie from the early 90's and, like me, fantasized about becoming part of Van Helsing's clique through the maddening chase for the infamous Count, this game is definitely for you. It looks decidedly complex, with all the different card sets and a host of colorful counters, but once you play through a few turns, it'll seem a lot easier and simpler than at first it seemed. That, alas, may be its Achilles' heel. Fury of Dracula, at its core, is a very sophisticated-looking game of Scotland Yard: a bunch of players try to move coordinatedly across a cool-looking board depicting cities of Europe, in order to flush Dracula (secretly moved around by one player) out of his hiding place -- whatever that may be. Granted, there are many perils to face aside from the maddening Train die, but they should come out more often -- zombies, vampires, human minions, even bats appear much less frequently than expected. And when they do, they mostly spit out a delaying special effect, then vanish. Where's the blood and guts? Where's the fighting glory? Worse yet, when you actually go head to head against an opponent, the fighting mechanic ends up being somewhat repetitive. Once you figure out the Item cards, it becomes a little predictable too. All in all, this game takes a few more hours to play than a game of this weight class should -- but boy, what a ride! Like I said, it's beautiful and any horror fan cannot go without at least one play. Lack of strong replayability is precisely what I fear the most. I will definitely research that with borrowed copies, instead of purchasing my own.

RATING: 6
A decent update of the original game.  Dracula has become much easier to find but much harder to defeat.  Some sense of mystery and drama is lost since the hunters almost always know where Dracula is.  I think the new edition actually goes too far in its quest for "balance", introducing a bunch of fiddly mechanisms and special rules at the expense of theme and gameplay.  It comes off feeling somewhat artificial and most of the new mechanisms up the complexity and length while chipping significantly away at the theme.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.15
One player controls Dracula, the other players the four hunters. Dracula must evade capture for six days, less if he can leave a trail of newly sired vampires behind him, the hunters must close in and kill him.
Dracula is moved secretly using location cards, the Hunters must pick up his trail and close in. But beware the game swings between Night and Day and in the Night Dracula can turn the tables with the hunters becoming the hunted.
Fury of Dracula is of course based on an old game, no not the original Fury of Dracula some twenty years ago, the classic Scotland Yard, in which team of detectives try to find the secretive Mr X on a map of London. Fury of Dracula is Scotland Yard with bells and whistles. 
So the game rests or falls on the basic premise of picking up clues about Dracula's (Mr X) hidden movement. In this the game surpasses the original. The use of cards to leave a trail is genuinely clever. But do all the other elements in the game overwhelm that central concept?
A little bit. Some of them, such as the rather involved combat mechanism to resolve an encounter seem convoluted (especially since there 20+ cards in the game required just to resolve a fairly straightforward paper-scissor-stones element of it). Likewise, characters are constantly cycling item and event cards throughout the game without apparently achieving anything. 
Some of the changes from the original (bites, vampires, weapons, etc) are thematically needed, some (such as Dracula being able to turn the tables at night) Scotland Yard actually needed to prevent the game becoming scripted, but a lot of what is here feels like hammers to crack nuts.
Had the designers made a simpler game they would probably have made a better game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.1
One of our first cooperative games, this is light hearted fun.  Would recommend this game to anyone who is looking for a quick coop game. (Did I really say quick , OMG! what was I thinking, having got several co-op games under my belt, this can in the wrong hands feel anything but quick and is not a true coop game as someone is always Dracula).
Having played this game on and off for a couple of years, I would say that the games can become a bit repetitive, but don't let this deter you from a very well designed and balanced game.

RATING: 3
I'm very surprised how highly rated the game is.  At first it seemed pretty good, although the odds seemed a little stacked against Dracula at first, and the fighting mechanic depends far more on dice rolls than strategy.  However, when I got into it, I began to see how the game balance worked out, and I saw the appeal of the game...to the human players.

The bottom line: it's no fun to play as Dracula.  You have very few choices, it's a long time between your turns, and for a dark monster, you seem to run away and get 'staked' a lot.  

I really wish the designers of the game found a way to automate the part of Dracula, like in Arkham Horror with the dark elder gods.  With this, someone's left doing almost nothing, and when it is their turn, they're in a constant state of retreat.  That's far from what I'd call fun.

RATING: 5
I really like the way Dracula's hidden movement is done, and how he places Encounters for the Hunters to meet when they come upon his path.  But that's about all I like.  The Hunters' actions, beyond movement, are often pointless - a lot of switching out items when they hit their max limit - and we particularly dislike combat - I was expecting something more like the rock-paper-scissor dynamics of Yomi, trying to second guess what card the opponent is going to play, but usually you just alternate between your 2 best cards, hoping to roll better. I don't like the die rolling at all in this case.  The theme is pretty well portrayed, but the clunky gameplay just prevents it from engrossing me, unlike for example Pandemic where the theme is more minimal but the mechanics are so elegant that at least I am able to really feel the theme when I'm playing it.  I still need to try Letters from Whitechapel - I hope it's much better.

Update: Letters from Whitechapel is much better.  Simpler mechanics, turns go faster. The way the detectives try to unearth Jack's path is more interesting than running into Dracula's encounters.

I love the game concept of hide-and-go-seek, strategy of what monsters to lay where and where to run, the rock paper scissor like figthing mechanism, the changing of power with the coming and going of daylight, and more.  It's a shame my group doesn't like this game more.  I recommend it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This is just about the best thematic experience available besides Battlestar Galactica. It's got such a great balance between solid intuitive mechanics and pervasive theme. The Gothic horror atmosphere is very real, and there is a tension between wanting to find Dracula, and not wanting to have to fight him. The balance is surprisingly sharp. Dracula is harder to play well, but when he's used properly, he dictates the entire flow and feel of the game. There's a lot of randomness associated with the combat, but I really like the feel, and it makes everyone think twice before engaging. One of the best games out there.

RATING: 8
It's a relatively easy game to master in terms of rules. It's also great fun to try to work out Dracula's location, close in on him and try to kill him before he can use his powers to evade the Hunters. The game ultimately depends on the skill of the Dracula player and the luck of the Hunters, both in terms of which cards they draw and which cities they travel to. Let me repeat: this game is fun and it's very thematic! While initially a little complicated, combat is fun too. The damage suffered by the losing combatant depends entirely on what both combatants tried to do during the fight, bringing an element of prediction to the game.

If you get easily frustrated at random card draws allowing Dracula to escape at the last second, I don't think this game is for you. And it can be frustrating if you finally managed to corner Dracula just for him to teleport to the other side of Europe.

RATING: 7
[3 plays, 5 player and 4 player games] Atmospheric and challenging collaborative game. In this genre, I like this better than Shadows Over Camelot. RATING: 7.5
I'm a big fan and owner of the original. I'm sorely tempted to pick this one up but have been rather disappointed by FFG releases of late (lots of bits and flash but no soul). This one has good heritage so it may come out well.

Then again, FFG didn't do so well with Arkham Horror so who knows?

UPDATE:

I caved and bought the new edition. Verdict? The game stays true to the original and has some well developed features. I like the new night/day conditions. I like the addition of Mina Harker for 5 players. The package is well made and looks handsome.

What did I not like? Well, I'm not a fan of the huge amount of cards the Dracula player has to deal with. I like the old screen (easier to manage. If a Dracula player cheats, that's just sad). I also imagined that the redevelopment would shave playtime but it's actually as long or potentially longer than the original. This is probably owing to the fixed Dracula victory conditions of getting 6 vampire points.

All in all, I would say that the new developments amount to a 10% improvement over the original and isn't really worth the upgrade for the owners of the original.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Here is another game I would like to be completely ga-ga over, but cannot. Production and theme are both very nice, and we all enjoyed the cat and mouse game of trying to pin down Dracula. The event cards, encounters, movement, and deduction aspects of the game are all fun and well executed. Combat is a morass though. Tedious, time-consuming, and full of checking for modifiers, etc. The game also suffers from being unnecessarily complex for the experience it provides, and too long. We played for three hours, at which point Dracula had two of the needed six points to win (the Hunters were able to diminish a strong early lead on Drac's part), and Dracula was at full strength. Especially frustrating for the Hunters: they had worked to get Dracula right where they wanted him, and he used an Evasion card which allowed him to "teleport" anywhere in Europe. So at nearly three hours, the game basically started over again. Argh! We could have played another good group game three times over by this point. This made playing the game feel pointless.

The rules, while being accurate, are not concise. Part of this can be explained by all the fiddly elements of the game which have to be explained: the day-night counter has to be moved at the beginning of Dracula's turn, and moving to Dawn causes the Vampire track and the Hunter's Resolve track to each increase by one and any Hunter can redeem a Resolve Point to do one of such and such actions, and during combat any Hunter can play a card to modify combat but only at the beginning of combat but only the combating Hunter can play cards affecting combat once combat begins and some encounters can be "matured" to provide extra bonuses for Dracula once they move off his Trail Track but only certain encounters, and Dracula has to play blood points to do certain actions, and so on and so forth. Even with all this, the rules were a bit frustrating. Reading through them, there is a lot of: "...which leads to combat - see page XX for a description of combat." If you are reading the rules trying to get a feel for the sequence of play, this constant "go look at page such and such" is a pain. All of this complexity is for a purpose: Fury of Dracula tries to faithfully recreate the environment of Stoker's Dracula, albeit ten years later. So it makes sense, for example, that you cannot travel as fast by train in Eastern Europe, as the transit system there was less developed during the period. Unfortunately, the complexity introduced by this kind of accuracy detracted from the game for our group.

Combat is accomplished by a combination of dice rolling and card playing, and not only dragged on for too long, but created very little tension. It is no surprise to see people inventing all sorts of combat variants. A system like that used in Lord of the Rings: the Confrontation, would have been really excellent here. Too bad.

Cons: - you may need to have the immortality of the undead to last through a game
      - a lot of complexity for what it delivers
      - combat not fun
      - unbalanced by a few cards
Pros: - dripping with theme - it really does feel like a hunt for Dracula
      - the combination of guessing and calculating to discover Dracula's location
      - beautiful production

To be fair, this is not a board game emerging from the European school of design, where complex strategies emerge from a simple set of rules. It's a big, messy American affair. The original came out in the mid-80s, preceding many of the favorite games on the Geek. I had hoped that this iteration would take advantage of recent developments in design, but it didn't seem to. I desperately want to love this game, but I feel as if I'd have to rework many aspects to get it to play in about 90-120 minutes: new combat system, revision of event card deck, reduction of fiddly simulation elements, and so on. Bottom line is we can have a lot more fun in three hours with other games. I'd like to see FoD get further plays, but I'm going to have to do a lot of convincing to make that happen.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Like most 1vAll games, the experience depends on the Dracula player. If he isn't tricky enough to present a constant feeling of challenge, then the hunters will get bored.

And even then the experience can be possibly lopsided. But when it works just right (which seems more often than not with competent play), this is a long, epic game that creates some great stories and feels pretty good to play, despite feeling a little underdeveloped by modern standards. The rules are so simple and intuitive and the concept and teamwork is enjoyable to the point where I'd almost call this a great gateway game, if it weren't for the length being off-putting to most non-gamers.

I really like the way both sides feel boht powerful and frustrating to the other. It really helps to create the atmosphere and encourage fear in both sides. Classic super villian vs hero thing going on, with each side one-upping each other all the time... but falling constantly one step short of actually defeating their opponent. 

As the hunters, you can know exactly where Dracula is, only to be crushed a moment later when he orchestrates a roadblock to cut off your pursuit, head low in his horse and carriage while you struggle with the obstacle. Or as Dracula, you can set up the perfect series of decoys for the Hunters, but the train delay works in their favor, your Minions fail you, and you end up face to face with a would-be-victim wielding a stake. Moments like these create a compelling narrative that directs your attention away from the fact that you're hardly doing anything on your turn, and that that's been going on for 3 hours.

[b]Player Counts[/b]: You may think this might work better with fewer players, maybe even 2 since there is less downtime and more for each individual hunter to handle, but increased fiddliness (managing separate hands) and lack of discussion  -- this game depends on a verbally active table, both for the benefit of Dracula overhearing discussion and for the spirit of teamwork among the hunters makes more players better I thikn.

(4 Design + 5 Enjoyment)

RATING: 8
I'm big on theme, and since this game just drips with atmosophere, I had a good feeling about it.  I was unsure if my gaming group would like it or not.

I brought it to the table and it turns out we all had a blast.  Yes the game is unbalanced and has some problems, but the adventure and challenge and sheer fun of it all overcomes those issues for me and my group.  The biggest design flaw that we encountered was the random flucuation of power based on cards and encounters; Dracula could draw the vampire spawn encounter at the beginning and lay it down on his second turn.  He could also potentially receive at any time the card that lets him teleport anywhere - his new location isn't really the problem so much as his old encounters he left, if he was undiscovered.

Regardless, we did enjoy Fury of Dracula, and if the game's concept and theme appeals to you enough, then you probably will too.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
FFG's botched re-design of the old GW classic, Fury of Dracula, a brilliant game which I have played literally hundreds of times, and one of my few 10s. My buddy and I played the new one 4 times before returning to the original, which we both agree is far superior.

Where did FFG go wrong? For one thing they took an elegant, map-based movement system, and replaced it with an abstract card-based system that is so awkward and contrived that it requires special rules and work-arounds for Dracula to do something as simple as reverse his course. For another, they took a clean, exciting combat system, and made it slower and more complex, but no more interesting.

I honestly can't find one positive thing to say about the re-design. The original was a far better game - I won't waste another minute playing this one.

RATING: 5
I recently started a game of Fury of Dracula (actually the third edition).  I've played many games since I last played Fury of Dracula and feel that is worse than I thought it was on reflection.  I used to rate it a 6 and have downgraded it to a 5, because while I might play it now, I would only do so with great reluctance.  

The game is overly long.  In either the new or the old version it is fiddly with unsatisfying combat.  I find that instead of it building tension, it tends to build frustration for both Dracula and the Hunters.  I don't know why this has become a classic and why it has lasted.  There are certainly many games that were better than it where the original design dates back as far that now languish in obscurity and that do not get these deluxe reprints.

RATING: 9
I'll tell you why Dracula is furious - BECAUSE MINA KEEPS KILLING HIM!!  That, and the hunters keep finding me, I mean HIM, on THE FIRST GAME TURN, including one game where he was discovered even BEFORE he had even had a chance to make his FIRST MOVE.  And yet I keep wanting to come back for more.  Despite the rather excessive length of the game, my wife and I have found it makes for a very enjoyable evening (or two) of gaming.  Our first game was decidedly one-sided as Dracula was discovered and defeated in a few short turns, but he learned a few things from that one and the second game was a four hour nail-biter which quite literally could not have been any closer (the very last die roll of the very last turn decided the winner, with Mina, of course, coming out on top).  [Edit: Mina killed me yet AGAIN, and once again the game came down to the very last roll of the dice!]  It might have been nice if the game was a little more stream-lined and quicker to play through (see the "excessive game length" comment above), but I imagine to do that would mean taking away some of its depth.  So if you have the patience to sit through an hour of rules explanations for new players, ten minutes of set-up time, and two to four hours of playing time, you might just find it to be worth your while.  (If not, then give "Scotland Yard" a try.)  In my opinion, it does a great job combining the exciting cat-and-mouse elements of "Scotland Yard" with a rather unique combat system, to produce a game of hiding, seeking, running, chasing, booby-trapping (that sounds exciting!), collecting, and fighting that is fun for both sides.  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 4.5/5  Total: 9/10

RATING: 6
This game has both good and bad points in my opinion.  The theme is great, and it is well incorporated into the game.  The bits are top notch and very practical.  The rules are also pretty easy to understand.  Early in the game it is fun as the hunters try to find dracula's trail.  Once the trail is found and extrapolated to Dracula's current position then the game gets somewhat drier.  I say this because once Dracula's position is determined, it's very difficult for him to get points via maturing encounters.  That's assuming he even has the encounters to mature for points.  Thus you have to resort to combat against the hunters and try to kill them as the only good source of points.  The combat, while simple, quickly becomes very repetetive as combatants keep playing the same 2 cards again and again b/c they offer the optimal possible outcomes.  Granted, I have only played this game once, but it left me with just a so-so feeling.  I am willing to try it again though.

RATING: 7
[FFG 06 edition] {Vampire; deduction, cooperative, secret-unit, angel-vs-devil; optimal 5p} FoD is a very thematic game. It has the elements that I like - deduction and cooperative.  However, the learning curve is quite long; it may need 1 whole game for everyone, esp. Dracula, to understand the functions of the cards, items and encounter markers. It's not easy to explain the rules clearly unless you are an experienced game host.

It is a game that is very dependent on the players. If the players are conservative and narrow-minded, it can become quite boring.

The down time can be strong with slow players. A minor problem is that resolution of a fight can take long.

The components are nicely made. They are very effective and informative. However, some tokens are too small, which has to be handled carefully.

Played twice now.  The deduction portions of the game are neat, and things like the mixed Event deck are very unique and interesting.  However, the game itself feels a bit dry and plodding in many ways, and the combat system just -fails- in my opinion. RATING: 7
This is kind like Scottland Yard with random events, fighting, and a lot of theme.  It's quite good but it's much too long for my tastes.  I did enjoy it though.  One thing that bothered me was Dracula's ability to easily escape by taking to the water.  Granted he loses health when he does that but he also stops the clock (prolonging the game) and he's impossible to trace when he goes to sea.  That leaves players scrambling to pick up his trail as soon as he makes landfall again.  It also seems subject to wide swings of luck.  Incidentally, the game is quite true to the characters and events that are found in the original book.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The theme is well-conveyed by the gameplay. 1-4 players are hunting Dracula across Europe, and a lot of exciting things can occur. No bean counting or wool trading going on here.

The meat of the game is solid, but missing some refinements that would dramatically improve it. Strategies are opaque and so the game can be frustrating for new players. For example, finding a sneaky Dracula can be quite difficult at first. 

Explaining combat card strategies beyond "roll high" to new players (when to use a gun, or Dodge, or when Dracula should bite) is also tricky. There is real strategic potential for combat, but it is explained nowhere in the rules and it is not obvious at all: like playing rock, paper scissors without initially knowing which beats which.

Long game, too.

In conclusion, this is a great game with players of near-equal skill levels. But if you're like me and don't have a regular group, this will not be a game you pull out much despite the juicy theme.

Rating: 9.5.  There isn't much that keeps me from giving it that final "10" point.  I think I have to chalk it up to game length.  But I'm big on theme-mechanics binding, and narrative in games, and this has buckets of both.  Years after first playing it, and several of these newfangled co-op games later, I just love this game.  [19-5-2011]

Letter Grade: B+.  There are other games that use a cat-and-mouse approach to game design.  Fury of Dracula, however, unites this style of gameplay with a host of clever mechanics; a well-designed map that rewards clever play (for Dracula) and careful teamwork (for hunters); and theme, theme, theme.  Minus marks for game time, lots of rules, and slightly-too-complicated combat mechanic (see comments below).  If you can negotiate these things, or are used to rules-complex AT games, or you like the theme, or you enjoy the hunt (or being hunted)--you're sure to find something to enjoy in FoD.  [08-05-09]

First game took about as long as one would expect.  It was good, though playing as Dracula I worried the hunters weren't quite having the fun I was.  Because I was having an absolute blast.  Even though I sucked.  No pun intended.  03-13-09: Discovered today that this works well with 2.  I'm not much of a person, generally, for deduction in a game.  This game works for me because it feels more like a hunt, more like following clues and drawing the net closed--or it feels more like slipping through narrow cracks and masterminding your escape.  How do you get back on Dracula's trail when he slips through your fingers?  Where will he disembark?  Or how do you cleverly position your traps for the hunters?  Where can you bury your vampire that it will escape their notice until it's too late?

RATING: 5
Fury of Dracula isn't something I was seeking out.  I had a vague idea of what it was and it didn't really sound that exciting to me.  So what do I think after playing?

The Good:  I enjoyed the team aspect of it, and working together to hunt down one player.  Sometimes I don't enjoy cooperative games as there isn't a real sense of competition when you're just battling a game state, but playing against Dracula avoids that issue.  I also enjoyed the Scotland Yard aspect of the game, deducing where Dracula might be and logically narrowing down his position.

The Bad:  Length!  The game is just too long, and it could have gone a lot longer.   Randomness!  There's just too much wonky going on.  At one point Dracula just teleported out of our search net... which ended up not being too bad for us, but could have doubled the game length.  There are just too many cards that can swing the game too much.  I don't want to invest as much time as this game requires only to have a lucky card draw determine the course of the rest of the game.

Things I could do without: the fighting system seems a little unnecessarily  complex.  And the game seems set up so that it requires multiple encounters with Dracula for the hunters to win.  I would have preferred some simpler combat system with a single big fight.  Or maybe just doing away with the fight altogether.  

Overall, I enjoyed our play, and I'm glad I played it, but it's not something I'd look to play again.  There are a lot of other games I'd rather play instead.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A good game that I don't enjoy as much as I should, given it is thematic, has a nice feel to the hunt and a surprisingly small set of rules. And why is like this? Mainly because the game blocks the hunter players to develop a real strategy, because:

a) You can never know what Dracula might have put in a city - the tokens, once used, return to the pile and can be taken again, later on, so the hunters are unable to take things into consideration, like: "He has used the rats, the saboteur and the fog two times, therefore...". No, nothing of this sort. I agree that the vampires that can maturate should return to the pool if found and destroyed, but until all the tokens are used (somehow), I think it would serve the gameplay better if they didn't return to the pool;

b) It is all on the dice. No matter how great the hunt was, nor how well Dracula has used his powers and servants to hide and escape, but once a hunter and Dracula are in the same place, all came to the dice. Roll poorly and you will lose, get bitten, die or Dracula will escape, no matter how great your hand is. The combat could be so much better, but inspite being somewhat novel (with its many relations between the cards used and its effects), I found it to be lackluster and disappointing - considering all the movement strategy that the game requires previous to the encounter.

The overall experience wasn't bad, mind you, after all I plyed with friends, with gret table talk cursing the devious ways of Dracula and his minions and the game does has an amazing feel of a hunt against time, chasing down a cunning enemy.

It just could have been better - probably and 8 or 8.5 if the combat system wasn't so much dice dependent.

RATING: 10
In this game of Gothic adventure, one player takes the role of Dracula while up to four others attempt to stop him by controlling Vampire hunters from the famous Bram Stoker novel.

Dracula has returned, and is determined to control all of Europe by creating an undead empire of Vampires. Dracula uses a deck of location cards to secretly travel through Europe, leaving a trail of encounters and events for the hunters that chase him.

Meanwhile, the hunters attempt to track and destroy Dracula using the limited information available to them - a task easier said than done when their prey has the power to change forms into a wolf or bat, and can even melt away into the mist when confronted.

To save Europe and rid the world of Dracula's foul plague, the hunters must destroy Dracula before he earns enough victory points to win the game... will they have enough wit and bravery to defeat the dark count?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
Unbalanced. Too reliant on knowledge of the deck and gimmicky card combos. Too many fiddly bits to keep track of that ultimately don't really add much to gameplay. 

I do like the tension of one side drawing cards and inadvertently powering their opponent, but that's about the only mechanic that I think this game implements well.

If you want a hidden movement game where the focus is on hidden movement, play Letters from Whitechapel. This is best thought of as an Ameritrash Adventure Game that happens to feature hidden movement as a mechanic.

RATING: 4
The game consists of tracking and deduction across a map of Europe. Player turns are short and can planned ahead, except for the Drac player. This game really needs five to play, or at least a group willing to marshall four characters against the fifth, Dracula. It all comes down to coordination. If the hunters are highly coordinated and willing to give up personal gaming interests then the only real hope for the Dracula player is to pull stunts like the Dublin Gambit (read threads on bgg). If the players are a bunch of self interested morons then Dracula will run around the board amidst the chaos. This feels a bit like an old game bridging the modern era. Fury of Dracula is not for casual or unfocussed gamer groups and it is seriously limited by the need for a specific player count.

RATING: 7
If you must own a deduction game, this should be it. It just feels great to work together with other players to find the location of Dracula, and the fact that encounters/fights can be unexpected and VERY dangerous makes it a lot more thrilling than most of its kin. The large amount of event cards and encounter chits also ensures each game plays differently. One of its best qualities, is that gameplay feels quite balanced for this kind of game, and the balance does not change with the number of players. In addition, turns are very short and the quality of its components is well above average (with great artwork). Just keep in mind that one game can take quite some time to play (and learn), and that the game requires a Dracula player who is willing to play less competitely if the hunters get more fun out of it that way. Otherwise, the amount of fun and suspense in this game might be a bit too dice-dependent.

RATING: 8
Very nice cat-and-mouse game.  Very tense if you're the Dracula player.  Can be boring for Hunters unless someone really keeps the game moving.  The Dracula player has a lot to keep track of - so he/she needs to be a Gamer.  Lots of thematic elements and immersion - especially if Dracula plays aggresively!!

Biggest downside to this game is that it takes too long - especially with new players.  Fastest game I've played (after 4 plays) has been just short of 2.5 hours, but each game has had new players and that time includes the rules explanation.  Shave 30-60 minutes off the play time and you'd have one hell of an intense game.

A lot of fun if you've got the time and are in the mood for a slow, simmering, tense, and teasing game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Luca Iennaco say.

"Debugged" version of the original (no more player elimination, more balanced cards, new movement rules for Dracula raising interaction and deduction, Dracula must play an encounter every turn).
Luck is still very important (dice and cards), but a bit less than before.
Atmosphere has been preserved.
Cooperation (with more than two players) and a bit of deduction embellish the game.
Very good with 2 or 3 players.
Average game lenght for us: 150 minutes.
Playing with all experienced players makes the game both shorter and more interesting (even if I think that it is biased towards the Hunters, it's quick and easy to regulate it with the hints given in the rulebook).
Some components (character sheets, box insert, lack of a cards/tiles holder) are disappointing given the price tag.

***Update (after 12 games): I've helped Dracula a bit, removing one copy of "Hypnosis", "Good Luck" and "Surprising Return", plus doubling the cost of "Resolve bonuses". The game feels better balanced now.***

RATING: 7
An excellent bluffing and deduction game, Fury of Dracula does a great job of keeping things tense and exciting. What makes it so good is that the heroes must not only find Dracula, but kill him as well. This raises the stakes (that's right, I said it!) considerably over other more typical cat and mouse games, like Scotland Yard or Mr. Jack. The heroes are forced to coordinate and plan their efforts to both locate Dracula and then attack him at the moment he is most vulnerable.

Using cards to track Dracula's trail is ingenious, although it does require a good bit of concentration from the Dracula player. He must remember what locations are in his trail and in what order they were visited. Failure to do so can easily give away Dracula's position and swing the game to the heroes. Combat is a bit wonky, but it gets the job done and is easy to figure out once you have been through it once or twice. Dracula's traps can be a little confusing as well, (particularly because they are also in Dracula's trail, and thus have to be committed to memory as well) and their effects can be pretty rules intensive. Thankfully, the rules for all of the traps are printed on the back cover of the rulebook and are easy to access.

Fury of Dracula beautifully depicts the characters and atmosphere of Bram Stoker's novel. It is decidedly more fun (as well as more work!) for the Dracula player, but if the investigators can get along and work together, there is also a lot of fun to be had for them as well. Like Arkham Horror, the game is even better if the group drops in some light role-playing to add to the ambiance. At any rate, it's a nice change of pace from the usual competitive gaming and a welcome addition to any gameday!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
"I am Dracula and I welcome you to my house. I must apologize for not being here to greet you personally, but I trust you've found everything you needed."

Beats the original GW edition by a few wolf whiskers.

[b]"I want you to bring me, before nightfall, a set of postmortem knives."[/b]

1. Superior art to the original (though I miss the charm of the GW edition).
2. Hugely better overall experience, mainly through the trail that Dracula creates in his wake. The Hunters are nearly always hot on the vampire's heels.
3. Allies for both sides. These are great: the Brides of Dracula and Sister Agatha spring to mind.
4. The Hunters cannot be killed off, their "death" only hastens Dracula's victory.
5. Accomodates 5 players, rather than the previous 4 players of the original.
6. Dracula has more strategic and tactical options than before.
7. Quality components. However I do not like the tokens that track day/night and resolve - swapped out immediately for gems.
8. Thematic experience game, resplendent with all the corny/great, vampire/Dracula lore you could wish for.
9. This version tracks Dracula's victory much more clearly than before. Originally, it was often the case whereby the game ended suddenly with Dracula declaring "I've won!" and the Hunters might not have known how far advanced his devilish plans were - this is not the case here now.
10. Good sized board - not too big or small. Easier to track the East-west divide than previously.

[b]Walpurgis Nacht:[/b]

1. Playing as Dracula can be stressful (the ever-present fear of cocking up the game by incompetent secret play).
2. The game is slightly fiddly.
3. Tactic cards are certainly not intuitive, confusing all who gazed upon them until a few combats had been experienced.
4. Long winded rules - took me 90 mins to download into my brain.
5. Minions instead of gypsies (so as not to offend the "Nation" of gypsy-folk, doubtless).
6. Playing Dracula well is more difficult than the GW edition.
7. Some of the card titles I liked are no longer present.
8. Castle Dracula is a teeny bit weak for my taste, but this is no biggie.
9. Scales lazily - by that I mean, all the Hunter characters must be included in every game. But this was a fault/wrinkle of the original as well.
10. Can play long - 2+ hours.
11. Some ambiguousness in the rules, mainly around combat and backtracking. Some situations were not quickly resolved - we had to ponder the ramifications of each interpretation of the rules - either way it could have gone in each case could have cost the game for one side or the other.
12. Requires some checking of what encounters and items do during the game. This will become less of a nuisance as more games are enjoyed.

Awaiting another play before reducing or increasing my rating.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Probably one of the better "all versus one" type of games I've played.  A good palate cleanser from the traitor mechanic cooperative titles like Shadows Over Camelot and BSG.  I enjoy the deduction aspect and unlike Pandemic, I feel that as long as you can think logically, you always have a way to contribute and thus it's harder for any one person to dominate the decisions.

The downside to Fury of Dracula is of course its length, which could probably be mitigated by reducing the number of VP required to win, or by increasing the points gained.  The other is that the combat is very difficult to grasp in the beginning, especially when and how a card is discarded after use.  Lastly, similar to the trapping of all GM'ed games, the experience is largely dependent on the person controlling dracula.  Taking too much risk may result in an unsatisfying session; being too cautious will most likely drag on the game for too long.  Therefore, he must make choices that will continuouslly let the hunters feel like they are indeed involved in a hunt rather than wandering around aimlessly.  So in that sense I think FoD probably won't stand up to repeated plays back to back.

RATING: 3
Boring, boring, boring, boring! I have played this game twice now, and the excitement at the table has been exactly zero on both occasions. I was with players who are great fans of the game, so they were enthusiastic about playing it, insisting that it is a good game. However the game feels like stumbling around in the dark, drawing cards occasionally. Every once in a while, you may be lucky enough to fight something with the confusing, unthematic, unwieldy card combat system! Then the game will end uneventfully, Dracula having escaped sheerly by virtue of the fact that all of his information is hidden, so there's no way to find him in most situations, except by drawing a lucky card. I see potential in this theme, but the game is dry, long, and too obscure in the information players have to make their decisions to make it much more than an arbitrary stab in the dark.

RATING: 8
1/02/14 -- This game is really fun with one caveat:  Dracula has to play more like a Dungeon Master than in competition with the Hunters.  How fun the game is is so dependent on the Dracula player keeping the players engaged, mainly by playing aggressively, laying a lot of nearby booby traps and only going to sea for special circumstances.  There is also invariably one hunter who is stuck on the wrong side of the board.  Dracula should do whatever he/she can to get that player into the game.  Because of these things, Dracula obviously needs to be played by experienced players (if possible).  Played this way, FoD is definitely a 9--an experience not to be missed.  With a competitive Dracula, the game's fun will fluctuate between a 9 and a 6 (a competitive Dracula can still lead to a fun game, but maybe only half the time).

---

12/16/08 -- Games of Fury of Dracula can run hot or cold.  Player experience, both with the hunters and with Dracula, plays a huge role the game’s energy.  The biggest bit of advice I have is for Dracula to avoid going to sea except in the most dire of circumstances.  It is almost never as good an idea as it might at first appear and also kills the game’s momentum.  Also, playing as a hunter against a Dracula player of inferior skill is usually pretty boring/unexciting.  I'm reducing my rating from an 8 to a 7.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
An excellent pursuit game. It roughly similar to Scotland Yard in that it features asymmetrical teams and hidden movement, but it's also quite different. There's a lot more interaction with Dracula leaving traps for the heroes and the heroes trying to capture and kill Dracula.

I quite enjoyed my first game of this and plan to play again in the near future.

After another play, I'm lowering my rating. This game isn't as fun as the Hunters since your options are basically move, draw cards, roll dice occasionally. The biggest problem seemed to be that there are very few ways for the hunters to actually catch Dracula, so once they catch his trail the game enters into a very long and drawn out process of them chasing him and easily killing any new Vampires while getting just enough cards to keep on the trail and keep Dracula from moving the game towards its end.

Basically, this game would be a lot better if it resolved quicker.

RATING: N/A
